**Attachment Reorganization.** Pre-morbidly likely *earned secure* or *securely-leaning*, Franklin pivots hard into a **fearful-avoidant (disorganized)** adult presentation: he simultaneously longs for and cannot tolerate proximity to the surviving attachment figures (Sue, Johnny). The avoidance wins, but it is not cool dismissive avoidance — it is anguished avoidance, which is why the alcohol is required to maintain it.

**Defenses Crystallizing.** Self-punishment as primary defense locks in during this decade. Reaction formation is not yet available (he is not healing strangers — he is not healing anyone). Geographic displacement begins. Sacrificial idealization has not yet appeared; it will require a stage on which to perform.

---

### Decade III — Carceral Stabilization (the prison years)

**The Function of Prison.** Prison is not, for Franklin, an interruption of his trajectory — it is its *completion*. The criminal exposure of the late free-fall was, behaviorally, a search for a container strong enough to hold the self-punishment that exceeded his private capacity to administer. The accidental killing of Logan provides the legal mechanism; the state takes over the punitive function. This is, in object-relations terms, the externalization of the internal saboteur onto an institution capable of executing its sentence. He stops drinking (institutionally enforced), stops gambling (institutionally enforced), stops fleeing (institutionally enforced). The decade of carceral life is, paradoxically, his first period of *behavioral stabilization* since Mary's death — not because he has healed but because the prison is doing the regulatory work his shattered self cannot.

**Affect Regulation.** Externally scaffolded by routine. The substance use disorder enters forced remission. Internal regulation likely improves modestly — sustained sobriety would permit some return of executive function — but no therapeutic processing of the trauma occurs. He is, in van der Kolk's idiom, *surviving without metabolizing*. The trauma is preserved in amber.

**Cognitive Style.** Narrowed further. Prison cognition tends toward presentism and concrete operations; for a man already arrested in self-condemnation, the environment reinforces the freeze. Importantly, **he does not appeal, does not write Sue, does not attempt to reclaim his license.** This non-action is itself a positive datum: it indicates a settled internal verdict. A man who believed himself innocent or recoverable would generate at least episodic protest. Franklin generates none. Seligman's *learned helplessness* applies but is insufficient — this is not helplessness, it is *acceptance of deserved fate*. The two look identical from outside and differ entirely inside.

**Self-Concept.** Consolidates into a stable negative identity: *I am the man who killed his wife and abandoned his children, and prison is where such men belong.* Erikson's adult crisis of *generativity vs. stagnation* is resolved in the stagnation direction, but with a moral overlay: stagnation as ethical obligation. He is not failing to generate; he is *refusing* to generate, because he believes he forfeited the right.

**Attachment.** Deactivated. The fearful-avoidant pull-push of Decade II settles into a quieter, more uniformly avoidant deactivation. He does not reach out. The longing is presumably still present but is so successfully encysted that no behavioral leakage occurs across the prison years.

**Latent Development.** Something quietly important happens in this decade: he survives. The body that ought, on his own internal accounting, to have been destroyed by now persists. This sets the precondition for the sacrificial-death idiom of Decade IV — he has been *waiting for the right opportunity to die*, and prison, for all its degradation, does not provide one. He needs his children's danger for that.

---

### Decade IV — The Sacrificial Reunion and Its Aftermath (the *FF* #32 era and the apparent-death interregnum)

**The Triggering Event.** The Skrull operation drags Franklin into proximity to his children for the first time since the rupture. Critically, he does not approach them; he is *brought*. The avoidance has held that long. When proximity becomes unavoidable, his entire psychological apparatus must produce, in compressed time, a resolution to a decade-plus of unmetabolized material.

**The Solution He Selects.** A single irreversible cut. The bomb. This is not a panicked act — it is the surgical idiom returning under its original valence (decisive, irreversible, in service of saving life), now applied to himself as the lesion to be excised. Note the structural elegance from his point of view: he gets to (a) protect his children, (b) be seen by them as good in the final instant, (c) avoid the months and years of unbearable sustained intimacy that any other resolution would require, and (d) discharge the guilt-debt in a currency he has been holding for over a decade — his own life. **It is the most efficient possible compromise formation among his competing internal demands.**

**Affect in the Moment.** The narrative shows tenderness — the final exchange with Sue. This is genuine and clinically important: it demonstrates that the warmth was never destroyed, only sequestered. Under the cover of imminent death (which closes the window on sustained exposure), he can permit himself the affect he has refused himself for years. This is the avoidant's bargain: feeling becomes safe only when escape is guaranteed.

**Defenses Newly Crystallized.** *Sacrificial idealization* fully comes online here and will define everything subsequent. Worden's Task IV (finding an enduring connection while embarking on new life) is bypassed by substitution: Franklin embarks on no new life and instead converts his death into the "enduring connection" his children must now carry. This is, in Bowen terms, a *legacy of unresolved grief* transmitted forward.

**The Interregnum (apparent death period).** Whatever interior experience he has between the bomb and his Skrull-medical resurrection is irrecoverable; what matters psychologically is that the *world believes him dead* and so does he, until awakened. His children mourn. His debt is, by his own ledger, paid. When he wakes, the ledger is empty for the first time since Mary died — and he must construct a new psychological economy for a self that was supposed to be over.

---

### Decade V — The Healer-at-Cosmic-Remove (resurrection through the alien-realm years)

**The New Equilibrium.** Franklin reconstitutes as a functioning physician in a setting maximally distant from his children. This is the most clinically interesting period of his life because it demonstrates what he is capable of when the conditions of his shame are removed: he is *good at it*. Sober, competent, tender with patients, useful. The collapse of Decades II–III was not characterological — it was the local effect of being a surgeon in the city where his wife died and a father to children who knew the man he used to be.

**Affect Regulation.** Returns to vocational scaffolding, exactly as in Decade I. Task-immersion as the regulatory engine. The substance dependency stays in remission because the trauma cues are absent. He has, in effect, reconstructed Decade I's regulatory architecture in a setting where the wound cannot follow — but at the cost of all the relationships that mattered.

**Cognitive Style.** Restored surgical competence implies restored executive function and procedural memory; the cognitive instrument was never damaged, only taken off-line by affective overload. This is consistent with the literature on trauma-induced functional impairment: the substrate is preserved, the access is disrupted. Remove the trigger field and access returns.

**Self-Concept Re-Stratified.** A *split* self-concept forms — the only way the contradictions can co-exist. **Cosmic self:** competent healer, morally serviceable, useful. **Terrestrial self:** still the failed surgeon, the killer of Mary, the abandoner. The split is maintained by geography. He can be the cosmic self only because he never has to be in the same room as the evidence for the terrestrial self. This is the classic Fairbairnian schizoid maneuver: the libidinal ego and the rejecting object are kept in separate compartments to preserve workability.

**Attachment.** Re-engages with strangers — patients, fellow inhabitants of the realms he occupies — in a *care-giving* register that permits intimacy through asymmetry (the patient depends on him; he does not depend back). With his children, attachment remains deactivated. The intermittent contacts during this era are brief, framed by crisis, and never extend to sustained domestic presence. The pattern: he will heal anyone in the universe except by being there for breakfast.

**Reaction Formation Matures.** What was raw self-punishment in Decade II and carceral stillness in Decade III becomes, here, *displaced restitution* — the doctor restored, but at the wrong address. Every patient he saves on an alien world is, unconsciously, an attempted partial-payment on the debt of Mary. The debt is, of course, non-fungible; one cannot pay a particular dead person back through unrelated living ones. But the unconscious does not know this, and the compromise allows him to function.

---

### Decade VI (compressed) — The Second and Final Death (the *FF* #377 conclusion)

**The Repetition.** The cosmic-conflict death is structurally identical to the bomb: imminent threat to his children, single irreversible self-sacrificial cut, tender final moment with Sue. The repetition is the diagnostic finding. Freud's *Wiederholungszwang* — the repetition compulsion — is fully visible: an unmetabolized trauma is restaged until either it is worked through or the subject is consumed by it. Franklin chose consumption.

**Why It Had to Happen Again.** The first death's debt-discharge was undone by his resurrection. The ledger reopened. The cosmic-healer years were a holding pattern, not a resolution; the underlying internal verdict (*I owe my life for hers*) was never revised, only suspended. Given sufficient time and the right precipitating threat, the verdict had to be executed. He was, across the entire post-Mary period, a man waiting for permission to die well. The cosmic-energy event provides that permission a second time, and this time the discharge is final.

**Final Affective Configuration.** In the closing exchange — again, tenderness; again, the avoidant's bargain (feeling permitted only with escape guaranteed). He dies regulated, coherent, and arguably (by his lights) at peace. This is the cruelest finding in the dossier: **the most psychologically integrated Franklin ever achieves is in the act of dying for his children.** Living for them was the impossible task; dying for them was the achievable one. He repeatedly chose the achievable.

---

### Cross-Sectional Synthesis — What Evolved and What Did Not

**What Evolved.**
- *Behavioral expression of the core wound* shifted from chaotic self-destruction (Decade II) to institutional containment (III) to single-event sacrificial discharge (IV) to displaced restitution (V) to final discharge (VI). The wound found progressively more *coherent* and less *socially noisy* forms of expression.
- *Functional capacity* recovered substantially from Decade V onward, demonstrating preserved substrate.
- *Defensive sophistication* increased — from blunt self-punishment to reaction-formation-via-vocation to integrated sacrificial idealization.

**What Did Not Evolve.**
- *The core internal verdict.* From the moment Mary died on his table until the cosmic-energy event killed him, Franklin's internal judgment — *I am the man who killed her; I owe my life; I cannot be in the room with my children as anything but a debt-payer* — never revised. No therapeutic work, no mourning task completed, no Kohutian transmuting internalization of the loss. The verdict is stable across forty-plus years.
- *The attachment deactivation toward his children.* It was never reversed, only modulated by context (deeper in prison, briefly suspended at moments of sacrificial proximity, otherwise constant).
- *The surgical cognitive style applied to existential decisions.* He decided his way to each death the way he once decided his way through an operation. The instrument was never recalibrated for the different domain.

**The Tragic Architecture.** Franklin Storm is a longitudinal demonstration of a single clinical principle: **a trauma that locks the self-concept early can be functionally circumvented but not undone, and the circumvention will determine the entire downstream life.** He built an elaborate, even noble, life around a verdict he never appealed. Everything competent in his later years rests on the same foundation as everything destructive in his earlier ones: the unrevised internal judgment that he had forfeited the right to be ordinarily present with the people he loved.

In Worden's terms, he completed none of the four tasks of mourning for Mary. In Shear's, his Prolonged Grief Disorder was lifelong and untreated. In Shay's, the moral injury was never repaired by the community-of-witness reparative work it requires (and which his isolation made impossible). In Kohut's, the catastrophic loss of the mirroring selfobject was met not by transmuting internalization but by structural collapse and substitutive scaffolding.

He died, in the end, as he had lived since the day Mary did: *a grieving surgeon who never left the operating room where his wife died*, who learned, over the decades, only to keep that room far enough from his children that they would not have to see him still standing in it.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Dr. Franklin Storm

*Prepared as a longitudinal forensic-psychiatric reconstruction from the full behavioral record (Glenville practice years through final cosmic death, c. 1993). Diagnoses are formulated to DSM-5-TR analogs with ICD-11 cross-references where useful. The subject was never formally evaluated in the canonical record; what follows is reverse-engineered from observable conduct, occupational history, carceral record, sworn statements made in his children's presence, and the testimony of his own body.*

---

## 1. Premorbid Baseline (Pre-Mortem Mary, est. age 20–~40)

Before the index trauma, Franklin presents — by inference from his accomplishments and the trajectory of his collapse — as a **high-functioning, conscientious, perfectionistic, emotionally reserved man** with no evident Axis I or Axis II pathology. The completion of medical school and surgical residency, the establishment of an independent Long Island practice, the sustained marriage to Mary, the raising of two children to early adolescence and pre-adolescence respectively — all of this requires sustained executive function, frustration tolerance, and capacity for committed pair-bonding.

Premorbid traits, projected backward from later behavior:

- **High conscientiousness** (Big Five C, top decile). Required by surgical training; consistent with the meticulous self-blame that follows.
- **Moderate-to-high neuroticism**, *contained* by occupational structure. Surgeons select for and require the capacity to bind anxiety into procedural action; Franklin's later decompensation suggests his containment was always partly scaffolded by his role rather than by internal resources.
- **Low-to-moderate extraversion.** Reserved affect, observed in every published interaction; the relational style of a man who connects deeply with few rather than broadly with many.
- **High agreeableness with a stubborn moral spine.** He does not argue his prison sentence, but he also refuses to inform on associates and refuses to use his children as resources. The combination reads as a quiet, almost Protestant ethical rigidity.
- **High openness only within domain.** Intellectual curiosity within medicine; little evidence of broader aesthetic or speculative interests.

There is no documented prior depressive episode, no prior substance use disorder, no anxiety disorder, no developmental history of conduct disturbance. The premorbid record is, in clinical shorthand, *clean*. This matters: what comes next is not the expression of latent pathology but the **shattering of a structurally sound man at the single load-bearing joint his architecture could not survive having broken**.

---

## 2. The Index Trauma — Anatomy of the Precipitant

The automobile accident and the operation that followed constitute a Criterion A event of unusually overdetermined potency. The trauma satisfies the diagnostic threshold for PTSD on multiple converging dimensions, which is rare:

1. **Actual death of a primary attachment figure** (spouse).
2. **Direct witness** to that death in graphic medical detail.
3. **Subject as the failed agent of rescue** — not a bystander but the surgeon.
4. **Possible causal role in the precipitating event itself** (variant accounts place him at the wheel; even in versions where Mary drives, the subject was present and uninjured, generating survivor-guilt overlay).
5. **Catastrophic role-collapse** — the event simultaneously destroys his marriage, his self-concept as a husband, and the foundational professional schema of *surgeon-as-restorer-of-life*.

This is what trauma clinicians sometimes call a **"single-event total-system trauma"** — one incident that does not merely injure a discrete domain but **invalidates every premise the subject had used to organize his identity**. There is no aspect of Franklin's prior life that survives the event intact: husband (gone), surgeon (compromised — he failed at the most personally consequential operation possible), father (now solo, in extremis), self-as-competent (refuted in three minutes of surgical time).

The choice to operate on his own wife — likely made under emergency conditions and conceivably forced by transport time and injury severity — is itself a clinical detail of the first importance. It is the act of a man whose surgical identity is so total that he could not abide handing her to another's hands. That identity is precisely what the event then annihilates. **The instrument of his self-conception became the instrument of its destruction.**

---

## 3. Primary Diagnosis

### Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.89 / ICD-11 6B42), with prominent guilt and self-blame features

**Justification.** The DSM-5-TR criteria require, at minimum twelve months post-loss, persistent intense yearning and/or preoccupation with the deceased, plus three or more of: identity disruption, marked sense of disbelief, avoidance of reminders, intense emotional pain, difficulty reintegrating into life roles, emotional numbness, life meaninglessness, intense loneliness. Franklin meets the criterion-A duration by orders of magnitude — his grief is not measured in months but in **decades**, sustained without remission until his death. He demonstrably presents:

- **Identity disruption.** The Glenville surgeon is *gone* and never returns in that form. He becomes — successively — a drunk, a gambler, a debtor, a killer, a convict, a sacrifice, a cosmic exile, a stranger's healer. The identity disruption is so severe it crosses into something approaching dissociative reorganization.
- **Difficulty reintegrating into life roles.** Total. He resumes the *technical* role of physician only when geographically removed to alien worlds — i.e., only when reintegration cannot include his actual life.
- **Avoidance of reminders.** Maximal and specific: he avoids the two people on the planet who most resemble Mary and whose lives are the ongoing consequence of her death.
- **Life meaninglessness.** Inferred from passive suicidality (criminal risk exposure), then active suicidality (the bomb).

The **guilt-and-self-blame specifier** is the operative qualifier. Franklin's grief is not predominantly yearning; it is predominantly **moral self-prosecution**. He is not primarily missing Mary — he is primarily indicting himself for her death. This phenotype of grief is associated in the literature with the worst long-term outcomes and the highest suicide risk, and Franklin's trajectory tracks this prediction precisely.

### Posttraumatic Stress Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.81 / ICD-11 6B40), chronic, with dissociative features (depersonalization subtype)

**Justification.** Criterion A is met overwhelmingly (above). Inferable Criterion B (intrusion) symptoms: he never speaks of Mary in detail across his recorded appearances; the silence is not absence of memory but suppression of unmanageable intrusion — the avoidant's defense against re-experiencing. Criterion C (avoidance) is, again, **total and architectural** — his entire post-trauma life is an avoidance structure. Criterion D (negative alterations in cognition and mood) is the dominant clinical surface: persistent negative emotional state, persistent distorted cognitions about cause and consequence ("I did this"), markedly diminished interest, feelings of detachment, persistent inability to experience positive emotions. Criterion E (arousal/reactivity): self-destructive behavior is explicit in the case (gambling to the point of debt, criminal entanglement, the killing); a foreshortened sense of future is implicit in every decision he makes.

The **dissociative subtype** is suggested by his later capacity to function as a competent surgeon on alien worlds. This is not a remission of PTSD — it is the **dissociated, geographically and ontologically sequestered** survival of his professional self in a context with no associative links to the original trauma. He can hold the scalpel again only where nothing reminds him he held it last over Mary's body.

### Alcohol Use Disorder (DSM-5-TR 303.90), moderate-to-severe, in sustained remission post-incarceration, secondary to above

**Justification.** Documented dependence in the Glenville decline phase; contributory to license loss; consistent in pattern with self-medication of intrusion and dysphoria rather than primary craving architecture. Importantly, the disorder **remits durably** once Franklin is removed from the trauma cue environment (post-incarceration, post-resurrection). This remission pattern is diagnostic: a primary AUD would not resolve simply by relocation. A **secondary AUD driven by symptom self-medication** does exactly that when the symptom load drops or the precipitating cues vanish. He is not an alcoholic in the characterological sense; he was a man drinking a wound shut.

### Persistent Depressive Disorder (Dysthymia) with intermittent Major Depressive Episodes (DSM-5-TR 300.4 / 296.3x)

**Justification.** The behavioral economy across decades — flattened affect, anhedonia, hopelessness about restoration, low self-worth, recurrent passive and ultimately active suicidality — supports a chronic depressive substrate punctuated by major episodes. The first MDE, almost certainly, follows Mary's death and runs continuously through his incarceration. Subsequent partial remissions in the alien-world arcs reflect *role-mediated* relief (work containing him) without resolution of the underlying mood disorder. He never appears euthymic in the published record; his "good" states are competent, not happy.

---

## 4. Comorbidity Structure and Sequencing

The four primary diagnoses are not parallel; they are **causally cascaded**:

> **Index trauma → PTSD → Prolonged Grief (with guilt features) → Major Depressive Episode → Alcohol Use Disorder (self-medication) → behavioral disinhibition (gambling, criminal exposure) → carceral isolation → chronic PDD → passive then active suicidality → repeated sacrificial death.**

This is a **single etiological tree**, not a comorbidity cluster of independent conditions. Treating any branch without the root would have failed. The clinical implication, had he ever been evaluated: trauma-focused therapy (prolonged exposure or EMDR) addressing the operative event, with adjunctive grief-specific work (Complicated Grief Treatment, Shear protocol), would have been the indicated first-line intervention. Pharmacology (SSRI, possibly augmented) would have been adjunctive. Inpatient stabilization was indicated at multiple points and never delivered. He received, in lieu of psychiatric care, **a prison sentence** — the carceral system's habitual mistranslation of untreated complicated grief and PTSD into criminality.

---

## 5. Symptom Presentation in Specific Behaviors — A Translation Table

Because the subject never spoke his symptoms in clinical language, his pathology must be read off conduct. Selected mappings:

- **The unprotested prison sentence.** Symptomatically: negative cognitions about self ("I deserve this"), foreshortened future, passive death wish, surrendered self-advocacy. PTSD Criterion D and PGD identity disruption.
- **The failure to contact his children from prison.** Avoidance (PTSD C), avoidance of reminders (PGD), shame-driven withdrawal characteristic of guilt-laden grief.
- **The acceptance of Skrull surgical reconstruction.** Submission to bodily violation by a captor; consistent with the passivity of severe depression and the dissociative tolerance of acutely traumatized individuals for further violation ("what difference does it make now").
- **The leap onto the explosive (FF #32).** Active suicidality executed in a frame that allows it to be coded as virtue. The clinical literature on suicide-by-sacrifice is small but consistent: severely depressed, guilt-burdened individuals with strong moral codes will often select **morally laundered methods of suicide** — police-suicide, military volunteerism into hopeless missions, sacrificial protection. The bomb is exactly this.
- **The later healing work on alien worlds.** Dissociative containment via task; secondary-AUD remission with cue-removal; partial role-restoration without identity-restoration. He is a *function* there, not a *person*.
- **The second, definitive death (FF #377).** Repetition compulsion in a Freudian-but-also-Janetian sense: the unprocessed trauma replays through reenactment until terminated. Having survived the first attempted sacrificial death, he had no remaining technology for being a father, and the second presented opportunity was taken. **He did not relapse; he completed.**

---

## 6. Course Over Time

- **Phase I (premorbid, ending ~age 40):** Euthymic, functional, well-integrated.
- **Phase II (acute, weeks-to-months post-Mary):** Acute Stress Disorder converting to early PTSD. Onset of heavy drinking. Initial withdrawal from children.
- **Phase III (decline, ~1–5 years post-Mary):** Established PTSD, Prolonged Grief crystallizing, MDE, AUD severe, behavioral disinhibition: gambling, debt to organized criminal figures, the killing of the loan shark.
- **Phase IV (carceral, multi-year):** Externally enforced sobriety; depression deepens in isolation; passive suicidality entrenches; complete severance from children.
- **Phase V (Skrull abduction and first death):** Acute crisis, active suicidality, "successful" sacrificial death.
- **Phase VI (resurrected exile):** Dissociative role-restoration as a healer at cosmic remove. Symptomatically: partial remission of AUD and acute depressive features via role and distance; **no resolution** of PGD, PTSD, or core self-concept.
- **Phase VII (final death):** Reenactment-completion. Sacrificial death, the only paternal idiom available to him, delivered a second and final time.

The course is **chronic, unremitting at the level of core pathology, terminated only by death**. There is no point in the published record at which Franklin Storm achieves clinical recovery from the index trauma. He achieves functional accommodation, twice, and dies both times before accommodation could ripen into integration.

---

## 7. Rigorous Differential — What He Is Not, and Why

A dossier of this kind must be as precise about exclusions as inclusions. Several diagnoses might be casually pinned to Franklin Storm by a less careful reader. Each is wrong, and the reasons matter.

### Not Antisocial Personality Disorder

ASPD requires evidence of conduct disorder onset before age 15 and a pervasive pattern of disregard for the rights of others extending across contexts. **Neither criterion is met.** The premorbid record shows sustained prosocial functioning across decades — successful medical training, marriage, fatherhood, community practice. The criminality is **late-onset, narrowly bounded, and context-specific**: debt-driven gambling and a single contextually situational homicide of a loan shark, with documented remorse and accepted incarceration. ASPD subjects do not accept incarceration without protest; they do not accept it as deserved; they do not later sacrifice their lives to protect others without instrumental gain. Franklin does all three. **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not primary Substance Use Disorder

A primary AUD presents with progressive use independent of triggering events, persistent craving across contexts, and resistance to remission with environmental change. Franklin's AUD is **reactive, post-traumatic, self-medicating, and durably remitted by cue removal**. The disorder is real but not primary. **Differential ruling: excluded as primary diagnosis; retained as secondary, in remission.**

### Not Borderline Personality Disorder

BPD requires a pervasive pattern, beginning in early adulthood and present across contexts, of unstable relationships, identity disturbance, affective instability, impulsivity, and recurrent suicidal behavior. The premorbid record shows **stable identity, stable marriage, no impulsivity, no affective storms, no parasuicidal history**. The post-Mary dysregulation is event-precipitated, not characterological — it has a clear date of onset, a clear precipitant, and a coherent trauma-linked etiology. BPD subjects do not function as competent attending surgeons through their thirties. **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder

NPD requires grandiosity, need for admiration, lack of empathy. Franklin presents as the **photographic negative** of NPD across every relevant dimension. He does not aggrandize; he abases. He does not seek admiration; he hides. He demonstrates empathy — the entire sacrifice arc is empathy converted into self-erasure. The sacrifices, importantly, are **not grandiose**: they are executed without audience-seeking, without preceding declamation, without instrumental aim beyond the immediate protection of his children. Narcissistic martyrdom advertises itself; Franklin's does not. **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not Factitious Disorder or Pathological Martyrdom

Factitious presentations involve manufactured or exaggerated symptomatology for the sick role; pathological martyrdom involves self-injury for relational leverage. Franklin's sacrifices occur in **genuine, externally-imposed, contextually-appropriate emergency conditions** (Skrull captivity; cosmic combat). The danger is real; the protection is real; the cost calculation is internally consistent. The pathology is not that the sacrifices are false — it is that **they are his only currency for love**. That is a different disorder of relational style, and it lives within PGD and avoidant attachment, not within Factitious presentation. **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not Schizoid or Schizotypal Personality Disorder

Both would require lifelong patterns of restricted relatedness or cognitive-perceptual peculiarity. Franklin's premorbid life evidences **rich attachment** (marriage, fatherhood, partnership), and his cognition is conventionally organized throughout. The post-trauma withdrawal is grief-driven and avoidance-driven, not constitutional emotional restriction. **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not Bipolar Spectrum

There is no record of manic, hypomanic, or mixed episodes. The gambling, while a classic hypomanic correlate in bipolar presentations, occurs here in a **depressive-self-destructive frame** — debt-accumulating, pleasureless, escape-seeking — rather than a euphoric, expansive, grandiose one. **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not Primary Psychotic Disorder

No documented hallucinations, delusions, formal thought disorder, or negative symptoms outside the substrate of his depression. His cognitions about self-blame, while severe and distorted, are **mood-congruent and culturally/contextually intelligible** — they do not cross into delusional intensity (he does not, for instance, believe he literally murdered Mary with intent; he believes he failed her, which is non-delusional). **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not Adjustment Disorder

Adjustment Disorders, by definition, remit within six months of stressor cessation or become reclassified. Franklin's symptoms persist for **decades**, with stressor permanently embedded in identity. He is, diagnostically, far past adjustment territory. **Differential ruling: excluded.**

### Not "ordinary" Major Depressive Disorder, single or recurrent, in isolation

While MDE is present, framing Franklin as simply depressed would miss the **trauma-and-grief architecture** that drives the depression. Treating the MDE without addressing PTSD and PGD would, at best, blunt his suffering without resolving its source. The depression is the symptom-level expression of an underlying trauma-and-grief disorder, not a freestanding mood disorder. **Differential ruling: present but insufficient as principal diagnosis.**

---

## 8. Suicide Risk Formulation (Retrospective)

By any modern actuarial or structured-clinical risk instrument (Columbia Suicide Severity Rating Scale; Beck Hopelessness; Joiner's Interpersonal Theory), Franklin Storm was **chronically high-risk from approximately one year post-Mary's death until the moment of his first sacrificial death**, and again from his resurrection until his second.

Per Joiner's framework specifically:

- **Thwarted Belongingness:** Maximally present. He has severed from his children, his profession, his community; he experiences himself as having no rightful place at any table.
- **Perceived Burdensomeness:** Maximally present. He believes his existence damages those he loves; his death will, in his accounting, relieve them.
- **Acquired Capability for Suicide:** Maximally present. A surgeon habituated to bodily violation; a combat-adjacent participant in cosmic conflict; a man who has already killed (the loan shark); a man whose body has been surgically violated by aliens. The threshold for inflicting lethal harm on his own body has been comprehensively lowered.

All three vertices of the lethal triangle were occupied for the majority of his post-trauma life. The sacrificial deaths are not aberrations from his risk profile — they are its statistically predicted outcome, achieved twice.

---

## 9. Etiological Summary

A premorbidly intact, conscientious, perfectionistic surgeon sustained a single catastrophic Criterion A trauma — the surgical-table death of his wife — which simultaneously destroyed his marriage, his core professional identity, and the foundational schema by which he organized his sense of agency in the world. In the absence of any intervention, the trauma cascaded predictably into chronic PTSD, prolonged grief with guilt-features, persistent depressive illness, and reactive alcohol use, manifesting behaviorally as occupational collapse, criminal entanglement, carceral isolation, and ultimately two sequential sacrificial deaths that satisfied both his unconscious need for self-punishment and his conscious need to express paternal love in the only idiom remaining to him.

**He is not, in the end, a complicated diagnostic case.** He is a textbook case of an untreated complicated-grief and PTSD presentation in a high-functioning professional, allowed to run its full natural course without intervention across roughly three decades, terminating in the outcome that course statistically predicts. The tragedy is not that the case is mysterious. The tragedy is that the case is **legible** — and that no one in the canonical record ever read it in time.


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — DR. FRANKLIN STORM

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across the surgical, decline, carceral, alien-exile, and terminal phases. Cross-referenced against canonical appearances FF #32, FF #1xx Englehart run, FF #377, and ancillary flashback material. Predictive confidence: high where event-class is repeated, moderate where extrapolated from single instances.*

---

## I. BASELINE — THE CALM STATE (when calm is even possible)

Subject does not exhibit a true civilian "rest state" after 19—, the year of Mary's death. What presents as calm is more accurately *low-load functional containment*: the subject is regulated by task — usually clinical, usually somebody else's body on the table — and decompensates within hours of being unoccupied.

**Postural baseline.** Tall frame held with a faint forward stoop at the shoulders, the surgeon's habit of leaning into a sterile field carried into ordinary standing. Hands held low and clasped at the belt line when not in use, palms slightly turned in — the residual posture of a man taught never to touch unsterile surfaces with his fingertips. When seated, ankles cross left over right; the right hand rests on the right thigh, the left often drifts to the ring finger where the wedding band used to be (the ring is absent in all post-decline imagery; the gesture persists).

**Gaze.** Long, level, slightly underlit by lowered brow. Does not scan rooms the way a paranoid man does; rather, *fixes* on whoever is speaking and tracks micro-expressions — the residual diagnostic gaze of a clinician. Eye contact held longer than American norms with patients; *shorter* than norms with his own children, a tell visible in the FF #32 reunion panels where he is repeatedly drawn looking past or down from Sue's face.

**Voice.** Low register, slow cadence, sentences front-loaded with the operative verb (surgeon's grammar: *"Bring me the saline."* not *"Could you bring me the saline?"*). Volume drops a quarter-step when the conversation turns familial; he does not raise volume under stress, he *lowers* it.

**Idle tells (calm).**
- Right thumb rubs the pad of the right index finger in a slow figure-eight — the suturing rehearsal gesture, fully unconscious.
- Periodic small inhalation through the nose, held three to four seconds, exhaled silently through the mouth: the pre-incision breath. Frequency rises from roughly twice an hour at rest to once a minute under any kind of recall stimulus.
- Tongue briefly touches the inside of the upper lip when assessing a person — a contained version of the lip-press older clinicians do over a chart.
- When listening, a single nod every ten to fifteen seconds, never two in a row. He does not perform agreement.

---

## II. UNDER LOW STRESS (clinical work, routine interpersonal demand)

This is where the subject is at his *best*. Task absorbs guilt. He becomes someone else's instrument — a function the surgical role legitimizes.

- Speech becomes more fluent, marginally warmer. Uses patient's first name unprompted.
- Develops a small reassurance ritual: a single light press of two fingers (index and middle) on the patient's wrist or shoulder before turning to the work. Not a pulse check — a *blessing*, secularized.
- Tolerates interruption well. Will pause mid-sentence to take a question and resume the exact clause afterward, a memory-discipline drilled by years of operative narration to residents.
- Humor surfaces — dry, self-effacing, occasionally morbid in the way only physicians and soldiers permit themselves. He laughs at his own line with a single nasal exhalation; he rarely produces an open-mouthed laugh in the record at all.
- Will eat standing up, holding food in the non-dominant hand, the dominant kept clean. Coffee taken black, lukewarm, in long pulls rather than sips. He has not been observed enjoying a meal in the canon; eating is fueling.

---

## III. UNDER ACUTE STRESS — NON-FAMILIAL (operating crisis, alien-world emergency, combat-adjacent)

The surgical self engages and the grieving self disappears. This is the dissociation that makes him useful in extremity and useless in ordinary life.

- Voice flattens further. Imperatives lengthen by one or two words to maximize unambiguity: *"Clamp. Now. Above the bifurcation."*
- Breathing slows rather than quickens — a paradoxical autonomic pattern selected for by surgical training.
- Pupils note as dilated in dim-light operative settings but the gaze itself narrows; peripheral attention drops sharply. Anyone needing to reach him in this state must enter his visual cone.
- Decisions arrive *fast and irrevocable*. He does not poll the room. He does not second-guess once an instrument is in motion. Witnesses repeatedly describe a sensation of being *operated on* even when only being spoken to.
- Body does not tremble during; tremor appears in the half-hour *after*, fine, in the dominant hand, dispelled by washing the hands at a sink for longer than necessary — the post-op ritual that doubles as a stress-discharge.

---

## IV. UNDER ACUTE STRESS — FAMILIAL (his children present, his children endangered, his children's gaze on him)

The reverse syndrome. Where clinical stress *consolidates* him, familial stress *dissolves* him.

- He physically angles a quarter-turn away from his daughter when she addresses him directly on emotional matter — the body of a man who has internalized that he does not deserve to face her squarely.
- Sentences truncate. The fluent operative grammar fails; he leaves clauses unfinished or substitutes a touch for the missing words (a hand briefly to her arm, withdrawn quickly).
- Eyes wet without spilling. He has a learned habit of looking sharply upward and to the right when a tear is imminent, which abolishes it through ocular mechanics — a trick from the operating room where one cannot break sterility to wipe a face.
- Will reach for a redemptive solution at the first moment one becomes available. The pattern in FF #32 and FF #377 is identical: presented with a high-cost, single-action option that ends his presence and saves theirs, he takes it inside three seconds of recognition. There is no deliberation arc. This is not impulsivity in the clinical sense; it is the rehearsed availability of a long-prepared answer.
- He will *not* ask his children for anything in this state. Not help, not forgiveness, not water. The asymmetry of demand is intolerable to him.

---

## V. UNDER DIRECT PHYSICAL THREAT TO HIMSELF

Largely inert. He does not duck well. He does not run. The Skrull capture sequence shows a man who allows himself to be taken with minimal resistance — not from cowardice but from a settled indifference to his own continuance.

- Will not draw a weapon. Has no record of carrying one even in carceral environment.
- Hands rise palms-out slowly when commanded; head bows a fraction. Compliance is total and unhumiliated — the bearing of a man who has already passed his own sentence and finds external threats redundant.
- Heart rate (inferred from observed respiration) does not spike under threat-to-self the way it does under threat-to-others. The autonomic system has been recalibrated downward by years of unconscious wishing.

## VI. UNDER DIRECT PHYSICAL THREAT TO HIS CHILDREN

Total inversion. The only condition under which the subject becomes kinetically dangerous.

- Steps *forward* and *across*, interposing his torso between threat and child. The crossing footwork is consistent enough to be predictable — left foot forward, right foot pivoting to square the chest.
- Will accept ordnance, energy discharge, or blade onto his own body without evasive motion. The leap onto the Skrull device in FF #32 is the prototype; the cosmic-energy interposition in FF #377 is the reprise. Pattern: arms out, palms down, body flattening over the source — a gesture half priestly, half the body posture of a surgeon shielding an open field from contamination.
- Verbal output in this state collapses to one or two words, almost always the daughter's name. *"Susan."* The vocative is the entire sentence.

---

## VII. INTIMACY — DYADIC, NON-SEXUAL

The hardest condition for the subject and the most diagnostic.

- Sits at a slight oblique to the other party rather than directly across. Will choose the chair, not the couch.
- Hands occupy themselves with an object — a glass turned slowly by the rim, a folded napkin creased and recreased along the same fold, the lip of a coffee cup traced with the thumb. The hands do not rest empty in proximity to a loved person; emptiness invites reaching.
- Listens more than speaks at a ratio approaching four-to-one. Asks medical questions in lieu of emotional ones — *"Are you sleeping?"* substituted for *"Are you all right?"*
- When the conversation approaches the apology he owes, he performs a stereotyped sequence: the upward-right gaze (tear suppression), a single slow exhale, and a *change of subject*, typically to the other person's present life. He never completes the apology in canon. Closest approach: the final-page exchange of FF #32, where the apology is delivered in the act of dying rather than spoken.
- Physical contact initiated only at thresholds (the doorway hand to the shoulder, the hospital-room squeeze of fingers). Sustained contact — an embrace held more than two seconds — is initiated by the other party; he receives it with a small involuntary inhalation and a delay before his arms close.

## VIII. INTIMACY — SEXUAL / ROMANTIC

No post-Mary record. The absence is itself a datum: in three decades of intermittent appearance across alien worlds, healer's quarters, and the redoubts of Nathaniel Richards' allies, no romantic attachment is recorded or implied. This is not asexuality; it is a vow he has not articulated to himself. The wedding-band finger continues to be touched.

---

## IX. UNDER GRIEF (acute and chronic)

Acute episodes — the anniversary phenomenon, the unexpected encounter with a photograph, the sight of his daughter resembling her mother — are managed by a stereotyped withdrawal:

- Leaves the room with a plausible task pretext (*"I'll check the equipment."*). The pretext is always functional, never social.
- Locates a sink or basin. Runs cold water. Holds the wrists under it for thirty to ninety seconds. This is the discharge ritual — the same gesture as post-operative handwashing, repurposed.
- Returns composed, with the next sentence already chosen. No reference is made to the absence.

Chronic grief is metabolized by *occupational substitution*. He cannot be idle for long without the substrate of guilt resurging. The alien-world healer arcs are not adventures; they are a man keeping his hands moving so the inside of his head will not catch up to him.

---

## X. UNDER VICTORY / SUCCESS

Anhedonic. A successful operation produces, at most, a long exhale and a slight loosening of the shoulders. He does not celebrate, does not accept congratulation with grace — deflects with a procedural remark (*"The team did well. Sterilize the room."*). The deflection is sincere; he does not believe success belongs to him. Any sustained praise produces the upward-right gaze again, this time for a different reason — praise is intolerable in the same family as a verdict he has already passed against himself.

---

## XI. UNDER DEFEAT / FAILURE

Calmly absorbed. Where most physicians of his caliber would litigate a bad outcome internally for years, the subject *closes the loop fast*: failure is filed under the already-existing master verdict (*I am the man who killed Mary*), and the new failure is just one more entry beneath that heading. There is no protest, no review, no displaced anger at staff or system. He accepts the conviction and resumes work. This is one of the reasons his colleagues — when he had colleagues — found him unsettling: he did not *suffer* the small failures the way a healthy clinician does, because the small failures could not approach the size of the standing one.

---

## XII. UNDER INTOXICATION (decline phase, on the record)

- Alcohol of choice in the record: brown, neat, glass held by the rim with the fingertips rather than wrapped — the surgeon's grip, preserved even in dissipation.
- Quiet drunk. Does not sing, does not argue, does not become amorous. Gets *slower*. Sentences extend; pauses lengthen. Eyes lose the upward-right tear discipline and water freely.
- Talks to the dead wife. Witnesses in the Glenville period reported a low murmur, head slightly inclined to the empty chair beside him. Not delusional — knowing — the addressed-absence of a religious man without a religion.
- Gambling losses concentrate in this state. He does not chase wins; he stays at the table until the money is gone, then leaves. The losing *is* the point. The card play is a vehicle for self-administered punishment that has the social cover of a vice.

---

## XIII. CARCERAL BEHAVIOR

- Did not appeal. Did not request a transfer. Did not, on the record, request a visitor.
- Worked the prison infirmary when permitted. Reverted instantly to clinical bearing. Inmates with chronic conditions were managed with a continuity of care exceeding the institutional norm.
- Did not affiliate with prison social structures. Neither preyed upon nor preyed. Carried himself in a way that produced a small exclusion zone in the yard — not deference, exactly; recognition of a man already serving a longer sentence than the one the state had given him.
- Slept on his back, hands folded on the sternum — the supine of a man laid out, not the curl of a man hiding.

---

## XIV. DECISION HABITS (cross-domain)

- **Latency.** Clinical decisions: under one second when the field is clear, indefinite when the field is ambiguous (he tolerates intraoperative uncertainty better than most). Personal decisions: bimodal — either instantaneous (the bomb, the bottle, the cards) or never made at all (the apology, the letter to Sue, the reclamation of the license).
- **Reversibility bias.** Strongly prefers irreversible options in personal life. The single cut, the one-way door. This is the operating room's logic misapplied: in surgery the irreversible cut is correct because the alternative is necrosis; in life, his irreversible cuts produce the necrosis.
- **Counsel.** Does not seek it. Has no recorded confidant after Mary. Will give counsel — extensively, generously, on alien worlds, to other people's troubled adult children — but the asymmetry is total.
- **Cost accounting.** Discounts his own future to near zero. A decision that costs him a year is weighed against a decision that costs him a life and the two are treated as approximately equivalent. This collapses ordinary risk arithmetic and is the single most predictive feature of his behavior in any high-stakes scenario.

---

## XV. SOMATIC SIGNATURES UNDER SURVEILLANCE

For a watcher's reference, the following would be visible at distance:

- The figure-eight thumb-on-index rub at rest.
- The wedding-finger touch at the empty ring site, frequency rising under emotional load.
- The pre-incision nasal inhale, three to four seconds, becoming hourly under recall stimulus and per-minute under acute familial proximity.
- The upward-right tear-suppression gaze, the most reliable single tell of suppressed grief in the subject's repertoire.
- The wrist-under-cold-water ritual following any emotional spike.
- The quarter-turn body angle away from his daughter during emotionally weighted conversation.
- The forward-crossing footwork when interposing himself bodily between a threat and another person — left foot lead, right foot square.

---

## XVI. PREDICTIVE NOTES

Given any scenario in which (a) one of his children is in mortal danger, (b) a single self-eliminating action will resolve that danger, and (c) the subject is conscious and ambulatory, predicted compliance with the self-eliminating action approaches unity. The subject has rehearsed this answer his entire post-Mary life. It is the only answer he has fully prepared.

Conversely, given any scenario requiring sustained, unspectacular, non-heroic presence — a Sunday dinner, a hospital bedside vigil for a recovering child, a slow walk through a grandchild's first months — predicted compliance is low. He will find a task. He will find a planet. He will, if necessary, find a bomb.

He is consistent. That is the mercy and the tragedy of him: the file practically writes itself once one has understood the operating room he never left.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — FRANKLIN STORM (SR.)
## Section: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

A surveillance file on Franklin Storm is unusual in that it must be assembled from four discontinuous life-eras, each with its own diurnal signature: the **Glenville Years** (intact family, practicing surgeon); the **Fall Years** (post-Mary, pre-prison); the **Carceral Years** (state custody); and the **Cosmic Years** (post-resurrection, off-world physician). The man inside these eras is the same man; the *shape of his days* is what changes, and the changes are themselves diagnostic. A week of observation in any era would show a person whose schedule is organized around one of two armatures — the operating theater or its absence.

---

### I. The Glenville Years (Pre-Mary's Death)

**Wake.** 0510–0525, consistently, without alarm by the second year of his residency and never returning to alarm-dependence after. He wakes on the right side of the bed, the side nearest the door — a surgeon's reflex, the side that lets you leave first when the page comes. Mary, observed in the household by domestic staff and later by Sue's recollection, kept to the wall side. The bed was made by 0530, hospital-corner, Franklin's hands; he did not delegate this. A bed is a thing you finish.

**Pre-dawn.** Coffee black, brewed the night before and reheated. He did not eat breakfast on operating days — a habit inherited from his own surgical training and the older rule that a surgeon does not want a full stomach over a long table. He shaved wet, straight razor, in a methodical pattern: right cheek, left cheek, chin, neck, upper lip, in that order, never varying. The shaving mirror was angled to catch the bathroom window's first light. He was out of the house by 0600.

**Commute.** Glenville to the hospital, roughly twenty minutes by car. He drove a domestic sedan, well-kept, washed Saturday mornings. He did not listen to the radio. The drive was the last quiet of the day; he used it to mentally walk the day's first procedure step by step — what surgeons call "the verbal." His lips would move slightly. Surveillance from a following car would record a man rehearsing a soliloquy no one else could hear.

**Hospital, 0625–approximately 1830.** Rounds, OR, charting, consults. He took lunch standing in the surgeons' lounge — coffee, a sandwich half-eaten, the *New England Journal* folded to whatever article. He was known to the nursing staff as quiet, courteous, exacting. He addressed nurses by surname-and-title in the corridor and by first name only inside the OR, a small intimacy of the working room. He did not raise his voice. He had a tell when displeased: a slow inhalation through the nose and a deliberate placement of the instrument back on the Mayo stand — not thrown, *placed*. Anyone who had worked with him for six months read that placement as a warning.

**Home, evening.** Arrival between 1845 and 1930 depending on the day's caseload. He came in through the side door, hung his coat, washed his hands a second time at the kitchen sink — a ritual hand-wash with the children watching, sometimes counting along — and only then greeted Mary with a kiss to the temple. Dinner with the family at 1930, household rules: no medical talk at the table, no elbows, Johnny's plate inspected for vegetables. He carved on Sundays.

**Children.** He read to Sue at bedtime through her seventh year — adventure books, the Burroughs and Verne strata, a curated romanticism that, viewed in retrospect, helped install in her the imagination she would later need. With Johnny (still a toddler in this era) he was less verbal and more physical: he carried the boy on one forearm while pouring his evening drink with the other hand. A photograph survives in family possession of Franklin asleep on the sofa with Johnny asleep on his chest. This is the only photograph from this era his children describe without complication.

**Evening.** One drink — one — bourbon, two fingers, neat, after the children were down. He read in an armchair under a green-shaded lamp until 2230. Medical journals on weeknights, fiction on weekends. He kept a notebook on the side table and made small annotations: case ideas, articles to chase. Lights out 2245. Sex with Mary was, by inference from later remarks, scheduled in the unspoken way of long marriages — weekends, mostly, the kind of intimacy that does not interrupt the working week.

**Weekend pattern.** Saturday mornings: car wash, yard, errands, a haircut every third Saturday at the same barber. Saturday afternoons: hospital paperwork at his home desk. Sunday mornings: late breakfast he cooked himself (eggs, bacon, the only meal he cooked); Sunday afternoons: walks with the family, sometimes the beach. Sunday evenings he was quiet, already in the OR mentally.

A week of surveillance in this era would record an almost monotonously well-regulated man. The monotony itself is the data point: Franklin's pre-trauma life was a tightly closed system, and tightly closed systems shatter in specific ways.

---

### II. The Fall Years (Post-Mary, Pre-Prison)

Every Glenville-era ritual inverts or atrophies. Surveillance would record the disintegration almost line for line.

**Wake.** Irregular. Some days 0400 (sleep-onset alcohol wearing off, a panic-wake); some days past noon. The bed unmade. He moved to the side of the bed Mary had used and slept there — a substitution observable in the indentation of the mattress and the placement of the alarm clock, now relocated to her nightstand. He could not lie on his old side.

**Hygiene.** The straight razor was abandoned within six weeks. Disposables, used past their working life, irregular shaving, a beard appearing and disappearing in two- and three-week cycles. The wet shave had been a ritual of self-respect; the disposable was a concession that self-respect was no longer the point. Showers became evening rather than morning — a depressive shift, well-documented in the literature.

**Diet.** Coffee and bourbon in the mornings. A diner two blocks from the apartment he took after selling the Glenville house — eggs and toast, the waitress (a Mrs. Halloran, by the few records) eventually serving him without his needing to order. He tipped well and overpaid; this is consistent — the guilt-laden never short the help. By midday he was at one of two bars or a card room above a tailor's shop on the same block. He ate dinner standing or not at all.

**Drink.** Bourbon, the same brand from the Glenville evenings, now consumed at five to eight times the prior volume. He drank slowly, never visibly drunk in the cartoonish sense, but persistently dosed — the maintenance drinker's signature. He was capable of operating a vehicle, holding a hand of cards, conversing in full sentences while blood-alcohol levels would have prohibited surgery. The tragedy is precisely that he never appeared, to a casual observer, to be *failing*. He looked like a tired man.

**The card rooms.** Three to five evenings a week. He played poker — five-card draw and stud — and lost steadily. He was not a bad player; he was a player who *needed to lose*, and other men at the table read this quickly. The behavioral tell: he would call hands he should have folded, and the call had the same quality as the OR instrument-placement — deliberate, slow, the inhalation through the nose. He was not chasing a win. He was paying a fine.

**Debt accumulation.** Logged in others' ledgers. He did not keep his own. He paid late, accepted extensions, did not negotiate. He did not ask his children for money — this is the load-bearing absence in the entire fall arc. A man with two living children of working age (Sue at this point a teenager, but with extended family resources) chose loan sharks over a phone call. The phone in his apartment was working. He simply did not lift it.

**The phone.** Surveillance of the apartment would record the phone ringing — Sue calling, persistently, over months, and later Johnny in his teenage years — and Franklin sitting in the chair beside it, not answering. He did not unplug it. He let it ring. The ringing was itself part of the punishment; he listened to his daughter try to reach him and did not reach back. This is, behaviorally, the most damning datum in the entire dossier: not that he was unreachable, but that he was reachable and chose silence.

**The accident with the loan shark.** A single event, not characterological. The pattern of his fall *led* to a room in which a man with a debt-collection mandate moved toward him; the resulting death is, on the available facts, consistent with a struggle and a fall, not a planned killing. He did not flee. Police records (inferred) would show him at the scene, seated, waiting. The waiting is the diagnostic. A man fleeing his life had been given a door out of it; he took the door.

**Apartment.** Two rooms above a hardware store. Mary's photograph in a drawer, not displayed. A medical bag, intact, kept on a shelf — never opened, never sold. The bag is the relic of the self he had been; he could neither use it nor part with it. This is the structural signature of complicated grief: the inability either to integrate the lost object or to release it.

---

### III. The Carceral Years

Prison reimposes the structure that his collapse had dissolved. This is, paradoxically, the most stable period of his post-Mary life.

**Wake.** 0500, by bell. He returned without effort to the early rise; his body remembered it. He made his bunk to a standard that drew comment from corrections staff — hospital-corner, taut, the old surgical tidiness.

**Yard and work assignment.** He was, inevitably, identified within weeks as medically trained and was used in the infirmary, unofficially at first and then in a sanctioned capacity. He was permitted to assist the prison physician with sutures, intake exams, the management of chronic conditions among the population. This was, observably, the only period in the fall-and-after years in which his hands were working as they had been trained to work. Surveillance would record a different posture in those hours: shoulders down, breathing slowed, the small forward-lean of the engaged clinician.

**Meals.** He ate. He had not, in the fall, eaten with any reliability; institutional food forced a schedule. He gained back perhaps fifteen pounds in the first eighteen months. The body, given a clock, will rebuild.

**Reading.** Library access. He read history — Civil War, primarily, and the history of medicine — and a fair amount of theology, which he had not read before. The theological reading is significant. A man examining the question of forgiveness is doing a specific kind of work. He did not become religious in any practiced sense; he became *interested* in the structure of expiation.

**Correspondence.** Did not write his children. Did not receive letters from them after the first year, by which point Sue's letters had stopped. He kept the early ones in his footlocker. Surveillance of the cell would document a small stack of unanswered letters, weighted by a paperback. He did not reread them often, but he did, on certain dates — Mary's birthday, Sue's birthday, the anniversary of the accident — take them out and hold them. He did not open them again. He had read them once.

**Other inmates.** Treated him with the deference reserved for the doctor in a closed system. He did not seek protection and was not predated upon. He spoke softly. He gave away cigarettes he was issued in trade but did not himself smoke. He did not gamble inside.

**Visits.** None on record. He had instructed, on intake, that no visitor list be maintained. This is, again, the avoidance.

**Sleep.** Better than in the fall. Worse than in Glenville. He woke once or twice nightly, consistent with the lifelong-from-this-point sleep architecture of the trauma-bearing.

---

### IV. The Cosmic Years (Post-Resurrection, Off-World)

When restored to life and relocated by alien benefactors to distant settings, Franklin's days reorganize around the *only role he can still inhabit without collapse*: the practicing physician among strangers.

**Setting.** Variable — a refuge world, a settlement, a station. The constant is that his patients do not know his name from before. He is a doctor with no history visible to those he treats. This is, for him, a livable configuration.

**Wake.** Early, by whatever local cycle obtains. His body imposes a circadian discipline regardless of stellar conditions. He has been observed adjusting to alien day-lengths within a week — the surgeon's adaptability to call-schedules generalized.

**Practice.** He runs a clinic. The instruments are unfamiliar; he learns them. He sutures with whatever the local analog of suture is. He sets bones, manages infections, delivers infants in at least one documented case. The work is, by the standards of his Glenville practice, technically modest — there is no operating theater of the kind he was trained to command — but the moral content is the same: a body in need, a pair of hands.

**Meals.** Light. He eats what is offered. He has lost interest in food as pleasure; food is fuel, taken when the work permits.

**Drink.** Abstinent, by all available indication, in the cosmic years. The alcohol was always reactive; removed from the cues of Earth and given work, he does not need it. This is itself diagnostic — confirming that the AUD was secondary, not primary.

**Downtime.** Sparse. He reads when given material. He walks, in the evenings, often alone, often toward whatever the local equivalent of a high vantage is. He looks at the sky. The sky in these settings is not Earth's sky, which is, presumably, the point. He is looking at a sky his children are not under.

**Relationships.** Cordial with colleagues, warm with patients in the moment of treatment, intimate with none. He does not partner. He does not, by any record, even consider it. Mary is the unprocessed center; another partnership is unavailable to him not because he has sworn it off but because the emotional bandwidth is occupied.

**Sleep.** Still broken. He wakes, in any setting, around the hour that corresponds to the time of Mary's death on the table. He has done this for decades. He does not remark on it. He gets up, drinks water, and returns to bed.

**Contact with Earth / children.** Episodic, mediated by cosmic accident rather than initiated by him. When the children appear, he is glad and frightened in equal measure. He treats their visits as visits to a man on parole: grateful, polite, terminal. He does not ask them to stay. He does not ask to return with them.

---

### V. Cross-Era Constants — The Habits That Survive Every Collapse

Certain micro-patterns persist across all four eras and would be the surveillance file's *signature* — the way a fingerprint analyst identifies the same man through every disguise.

- **The nasal inhalation before a hard decision.** Visible in the OR, at the poker table, in the prison infirmary, on alien worlds. The same slow draw of breath through the nose, the same half-second of held stillness, the action that follows.

- **The deliberate placement of objects.** Instruments, cards, cups, scalpels-of-whatever-metal. He does not set things down; he *places* them. The surgeon's hand never lost the discipline. Even in the fall years, drunk and ruined, he placed his glass on the bar with care.

- **The wash before contact.** He washes his hands before touching any person he is about to attend to — a patient, a child, a body in the street. This survived the fall (he washed before sitting at the card table, an oddity noted by other players) and is unbroken in the cosmic years.

- **The avoidance of mirrors.** Post-Mary, sustained. He shaves looking at the lower third of his face. He does not meet his own eyes. The Skrull surgical alterations to his face — the taking and restoring of it — would have been, internally, almost a relief: a literalization of a feeling he had carried since he stood up from Mary's table.

- **The unworn wedding ring, kept.** On a chain, in a pocket, in a drawer — its location varies, its presence does not. He has never worn it after her death and has never been without it.

- **The 0300-ish wake.** The hour-of-Mary wake. Across decades, across continents, across worlds.

- **The refusal to initiate contact with his children.** This is the load-bearing constant. In every era — fall, prison, cosmic — the same negative space. He responds when reached; he does not reach. Every meeting with Sue and Johnny in the post-Mary record is one they engineered or chance imposed.

- **The willingness to die for them on first opportunity.** The other load-bearing constant, and the inverse-image of the first. The man who would not pick up the phone will jump on the bomb. A surveillance file capturing both behaviors in the same dossier would, if read by a stranger, suggest two different men. It is one man. The two behaviors are the same behavior. They are both ways of not having to sit at the breakfast table.

---

### VI. A Composite Week, Cosmic Era — What Surveillance Would Actually Record

*Day 1.* Wake pre-dawn local. Wash. Clinic by first light. Eleven patients before midday — a fracture, two respiratory cases, a child with a parasitic infection he treats with a local pharmacopeia he has learned. Standing lunch. Six more patients. Walks at dusk to the ridge. Reads by lamp. Sleeps at the third hour after dark. Wakes once.

*Day 2.* As Day 1. A surgical case — abscess drainage. He is observably more himself in the procedure than out of it. Returns to quarters quieter than usual after; the work of cutting has stirred something. Drinks water, not anything else. Sleeps poorly.

*Day 3.* A day off, by the local cycle. He does not rest. He inventories the clinic's supplies, repairs an instrument, reorganizes a shelf. The inability to rest is itself the symptom; idle time is dangerous time, time in which Mary returns.

*Day 4.* Routine. A letter or message arrives through cosmic channels — news of his children, perhaps. He reads it twice. He does not reply that day. He may not reply at all. He keeps it.

*Day 5.* A patient dies. He sits with the family. He says little. He does not weep in their presence; he weeps, briefly, alone, after. The dying-on-his-watch is the one thing he cannot fully metabolize even now, and surveillance would record a small, contained, almost ritual grief — five minutes, the heel of the hand to the eye, then standing, then back to work.

*Day 6.* Recovery day, behaviorally. He is quieter. He eats less. He walks farther in the evening.

*Day 7.* Returns to baseline. The cycle resumes.

A week of him, in any era, would teach the watcher this: Franklin Storm is a man whose days are organized so that he is never alone with himself for longer than he can bear. In Glenville, the family did this work. In the fall, the bar and the table did it. In prison, the bell did it. On alien worlds, the patients do it. Strip any of these armatures away and he collapses inward toward the one room he has never left — the operating room in which his wife died under his hands.

Everything else he does, every day of every year, is the elaborate furniture he arranges around that room so that he does not have to look directly into it.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Dossier Section 6. Cross-reference: Sections 1 (History), 3 (Psychological), 5 (Personality).*

The subject's family map is small, attenuated, and asymmetrically weighted. Franklin Storm has, across the published record, four primary blood ties of operational significance — his late wife Mary, his daughter Susan, his son Johnathan, and his grandson Franklin Benjamin Richards (the namesake) — plus a thin, mostly inferential layer of origin-of-origin (his own parents, his in-laws) and one quasi-familial bond, his son-in-law Reed Richards, which functions structurally as a surrogate-son / replacement-self relationship and is treated here because it cannot be understood outside the family system. Each bond is mapped below according to its longitudinal trajectory, its dynamic signature, the trust and safety it affords, the manner in which it fails, and the leverage it represents to a hostile actor.

What unifies all of them is a single distortion: every Storm family relationship is mediated by an absence — usually Franklin's own — which functions as a third presence in the room. He is rarely *with* the family member he is engaging; he is with them and with Mary's death simultaneously, and the death gets the larger share of his attention.

---

## 6.1 — MARY STORM (née unknown). Wife. Deceased.

**Status:** Deceased, pre-publication. Killed in an automobile accident on Long Island, exsanguinated or otherwise lost on Franklin's operating table during the emergency surgery he insisted on performing (variant accounts: in some recountings she is fatally injured before he reaches the table; in others he believes, perhaps incorrectly, that a different surgical decision would have saved her). The factual ambiguity is itself meaningful — *Franklin* does not hold the ambiguity. In his own mind the verdict is settled.

**History.** The pre-trauma marriage is reconstructable only by inference, but the inferences are strong. Franklin's pre-fall trajectory — surgeon in good standing in a respectable Long Island town, two children spaced for a stable household, sufficient income for the kind of suburban life that produces a daughter capable of running a household at fourteen and a son who grows up assuming his sister is his mother — describes a marriage that was the structural keel of a high-functioning life. Mary was, behaviorally inferable from what her absence does, the regulating presence in the household: the person whose maintenance of the domestic field allowed Franklin's surgical perfectionism to exist without consuming everyone around it. The fact that her death immediately liberates every dysfunction Franklin had been holding in check — drinking, gambling, criminal entanglement, paternal abdication — indicates that she was actively containing all of it, in vivo, every day, by being there.

**Dynamic.** Idealized retrospectively. There is no canonical evidence of marital conflict, infidelity, ambivalence, or even ordinary friction; the relationship exists in Franklin's interior only as a perfected object he destroyed. This is itself diagnostic — real marriages contain irritation, and the absence of any irritation in his memory of Mary indicates that the memory has been polished by guilt into a single luminous accusation. He does not remember Mary; he remembers what he took from his children.

**Trust / Safety.** Total, while she lived; this can be inferred from the magnitude of the collapse on her loss. Only a person who has externalized their psychic regulation onto a spouse collapses that completely when the spouse is removed. Franklin trusted Mary not merely as a partner but as the organ of his stability.

**Evolution Post-Mortem.** Mary's presence in Franklin's life does not diminish with time; it intensifies and becomes more abstract. By the carceral period she is no longer a remembered woman with specific habits, smells, jokes, preferences — she is a verdict. By the alien-healer period she is invoked, when invoked at all, as a justification for staying away. By the second death she has become indistinguishable from his own conscience.

**Failure Mode.** The relationship's failure is its founding event and cannot be undone. The continuing failure is Franklin's refusal to let Mary die *all the way* — to mourn her into a tolerable memory and resume the life she shared with him. He keeps her acutely dead, perpetually on the table, so that he can keep paying.

**Leverage.** Maximal. Any operator wishing to move Franklin in any direction would invoke Mary. Her name spoken aloud by a stranger would produce one of two responses: complete shutdown or complete compliance. He has no defenses here because he has never built any — the wound is maintained, not healed. The Skrulls did not need this lever because they had a cruder one (his children's lives); a more sophisticated adversary would not have needed to abduct him at all.

---

## 6.2 — SUSAN STORM. Daughter. Living.

**Status:** Alive. Adult. Founding member, Fantastic Four. Married to Reed Richards. Mother to Franklin Benjamin and Valeria. The primary surviving recipient of Franklin's love and the primary witness to every iteration of his failure.

**History.** Born to a stable home; loses her mother in early-to-mid adolescence; effectively loses her father immediately afterward, though he remains physically alive and intermittently in proximity. Inherits, without negotiation, the running of the household and the raising of her younger brother. This is the foundational fact of Sue's life that Franklin both produced and never directly acknowledged: he made his teenage daughter into the parent of his son, and then he disappeared further, into bars and prison, while she did the work he refused. Everything later visible in Sue — her competence under pressure, her tendency to absorb others' damage silently, her difficulty asking for help, her overdeveloped sense of responsibility for the men in her orbit (Johnny, Reed, Ben, Namor's intrusions, eventually her son) — is a direct legacy of the household Franklin abandoned to her.

**Dynamic.** Asymmetric and grief-soaked. Franklin loves Sue with an intensity that is observable only at the moments of his disappearance or death — his sacrifices are aimed at her, his last words are addressed to her, his attempts at restitution are calibrated to her face. He does not, however, *engage* her in the ordinary register. He does not ask her about her marriage, her work, her interior life, her grief for her mother, her resentments of him. He cannot, because doing so would require sitting in the room with the daughter he failed long enough to be seen by her.

Sue's posture toward him, across the canon, is a complicated thing: she forgives him before he asks, repeatedly, which is its own indictment — it is the forgiveness of a person who long ago stopped expecting the apology to come in a form she could refuse. She holds him as he dies, twice. She does not, on the record, ever fully express anger at him. This is not evidence of an absence of anger; it is evidence of a daughter who learned at fourteen that there was no adult available to receive her anger and who has not, in the decades since, found a safe occasion to deliver it.

**Trust / Safety.** Sue trusts Franklin's love and does not trust his presence. She has organized her adult life around partners who *stay* — Reed's emotional unavailability is at least geographically reliable, and Ben's loyalty is absolute — which is the corrective architecture of a woman raised by a vanishing father.
