- **Post-incarceration:** no recorded financial recovery. No prison-labor savings invested. No request for support from the now-famous Fantastic Four (a stream he could have tapped with a single phone call; he does not).
- **Cosmic-era:** lives outside any monetary economy. The alien stations provision him. He owns nothing. The vow-of-poverty texture of this period is not religious — it is the natural endpoint of a man who has decided he is not entitled to accumulate.

The forensic accountant's summary: **a complete asset-strip executed by the subject upon himself, using gambling as the disposal mechanism.** This is consistent with self-punishment as primary defense.

---

### 7.5 Infrastructure

He maintains essentially **none**. This is itself a profile:

- **No safehouse.** When in trouble, he goes to a bar, a card room, eventually a cell. He does not establish a fallback location.
- **No cache.** No documents, currency, or instruments stashed against future need.
- **No comms protocol with his children.** No dead-drop, no agreed signal, no "if-you-ever-need-me" channel. The absence is total and is the single most telling infrastructural fact in the file.
- **No legal apparatus.** No retained counsel of record post-conviction. No will updated. No medical directive lodged.
- **No social infrastructure.** No surviving close friends from the Glenville era who remain in contact. He has burned every soft landing.

The one infrastructural element he *does* maintain, late in life, is **a workable medical practice on alien soil** — instruments, theatre, staff or analogs. He builds infrastructure only when it serves the displaced-restitution function (healing strangers). He never builds infrastructure that would support a return to his family.

---

### 7.6 Patterns of Action — Longitudinal Behavioral Regularities

Aggregating across the full record, the following recur with sufficient consistency to constitute a behavioral fingerprint:

1. **Approach-Avoid Cycle on his children.** Every documented Sue-and-Franklin encounter shows the same waveform: a brief approach (sometimes coerced by circumstance, as with the Skrull plot), a tender moment of contact, an exit via crisis. He has never sustained a contact with his daughter that he chose freely, initiated, and ended without an external precipitating event.
2. **Self-handicapping before high-stakes engagement.** In the periods preceding the FF reunion, his behavior degrades further (deeper gambling, sloppier criminal exposure). The subject manufactures conditions in which any reunion will be on terms maximally humiliating to himself — which both confirms his verdict and gives him a reason not to stay.
3. **Refusal of recognition.** Sue and Johnny offer recognition multiple times across the canon — recognition as her father, as the man she remembers, as a member of the family. Franklin deflects each offer, usually by redirecting to the urgent operational task in front of them (a patient, a threat, a sacrifice). The deflection is reliable enough to script.
4. **Acceptance of false identities imposed by others.** Skrull facial reconstruction; "convict"; "alien healer." He accepts each. He resists none. The pattern indicates a man whose own claimed identity has so thoroughly collapsed that he will wear whatever face is handed to him, provided it is not "father."
5. **Heroism only in single-event format.** All recorded heroic acts are singular, discrete, terminal. He does not perform the iterated low-grade heroism of presence. The action-format he selects is, again, the surgical cut: one moment, full commitment, irreversible.
6. **No retaliation.** Against the loan sharks, against the Skrulls, against the system that imprisoned him, against the universe — Franklin does not retaliate. The absence of any retaliatory impulse across the full file rules out a large family of psychological profiles and confirms the inward-pointing structure of his aggression.

---

### 7.7 Signature Operational Tells

These are the **micro-signatures** — the details a surveillance file accumulates after long observation — by which Franklin Storm can be identified across cover identities and changed faces:

- **Hand-washing ritual.** Surgeon-grade hand hygiene, retained for life. Even in the gambling rooms, the cell, the alien clinic — the same scrub sequence, the same attention to nail beds, the same forearm sweep. A pre-Mary somatic habit that survived the personality collapse. The hands remember what the man cannot.
- **The half-second pause before entering a room containing his daughter.** Documented in flashback panels and reunion sequences: a perceptible hitch at the threshold. He has to assemble himself to cross it.
- **Eyes-down at moments of tenderness.** When Sue addresses him with affection, his gaze drops. The shame-response is reflexive, not staged.
- **Use of formal address.** He calls Sue "Susan" in moments of high emotion — the formal name, the name on the birth certificate, the name *he* gave her — rather than the diminutive. This is the verbal tic of a man reasserting a paternal identity in the moments he most fears he has forfeited it.
- **Reflexive medical triage in any emergency.** Before any other action — combat, flight, speech — he assesses injuries in the room. Persists across cosmic and terrestrial settings. This is the one piece of his pre-Mary self that operates without his permission.
- **The dropped sentence.** In dialogue with his children, he frequently abandons sentences mid-clause. Almost never with patients or strangers. The truncation is specifically attached to filial proximity and is a marker of intent-collapse under emotional load.
- **Refusal of payment.** When functioning as a healer (Earth-era pre-collapse and alien-era post-resurrection), Franklin does not negotiate fees, does not bill, does not accept gifts. The pattern intensified post-Mary. He renders the service and walks. He does not believe himself entitled to be compensated for what he can do with his hands — restitution does not invoice.
- **Body interposition reflex.** In any room where Sue is present and a kinetic threat appears, Franklin's first physical movement is to place his body between her and the threat. Observable in micro-gesture before he is consciously aware of the threat's nature. The reflex is faster than his deliberation.
- **No photographs.** No record of Franklin carrying images of Mary or the children in the collapse era. The standard sentimental object of the bereaved is absent. He has either destroyed them or refused to carry them; either way the choice is a tell — he does not allow himself the comfort.
- **Anniversary opacity.** No canonical observation of the Mary-anniversary by visible ritual. The grief is total enough that it does not require a calendar. Every day is the anniversary; therefore no day is.
- **Choice of standing positions.** In group scenes he gravitates to the perimeter, near exits, with sightlines on Sue but not adjacent to her. The standard positional grammar of a man who has decided he is a guest in his own family.
- **Speech pace.** Slowed in family contexts, normal in clinical contexts, accelerated in operational crisis. The pace tracks where his competence-identity is engaged: fast where he is fluent, slow where he is ashamed.

---

### 7.8 Operational Vulnerabilities (Predictive)

For a file of this kind, the exploitable vectors must be named:

- **Children-as-leverage.** Demonstrated by the Skrulls in *FF* #32. Any actor with access to Sue or Johnny can move Franklin without negotiation. He has no countervailing self-preservation instinct to resist this lever.
- **Surgical-failure scenario.** Presenting Franklin with a dying woman on a table, particularly under conditions reminiscent of the Mary event, would likely cause acute decompensation. Operationally: he could be neutralized non-violently by the right clinical tableau.
- **Mary's memory weaponized.** Any actor possessing detailed knowledge of the Mary event could destabilize him through controlled disclosure. The wound is unhealed and the scab is thin.
- **Recognition as father.** Paradoxically, being *seen and named as father* by Sue in a sustained, non-emergency context is operationally aversive to him — he will flee or convert the scene to crisis. A hostile actor wanting him gone need only stage warmth.

---

### 7.9 Operational Summary

Franklin Storm operates as **a one-man retreating column**. His tradecraft is the tradecraft of orderly withdrawal: burn the assets, destroy the documents, abandon the position, leave nothing for the family to inherit but the ground his body covered. His methods are surgical — single-pass, irreversible, executed without consultation. His infrastructure is null because infrastructure implies a future he does not believe himself entitled to. His finances are an asset-strip he performed on himself. His patterns are predictable to the point of scriptability, and his tells — the hand-wash, the dropped sentence, the body interposed before thought — are the somatic residue of two identities (*surgeon* and *father*) that he has spent the rest of his life trying to keep in separate rooms.

He is, in operational shorthand, **a man whose entire tradecraft is the management of his own exit.** Everything he does, he does to leave more cleanly.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — DR. FRANKLIN STORM

*A reconstruction of the internal architecture by which the subject reads the world and decides what to do in it. Derived from the longitudinal behavioral record; substantiated against the canon; expressed as he would express it to himself, in the dark, sober, at 3 a.m.*

---

## I. FIRST PRINCIPLES — The Axioms Beneath Everything

Every operational code rests on a small number of root statements the subject treats as self-evident. Franklin Storm's are unusually few, unusually consistent, and unusually punitive.

**Axiom 1 — Mortality is a problem with a procedure.** This is the surgeon's metaphysic and Franklin held it absolutely until the night Mary went onto his table. Disease, injury, death — these are not metaphysical mysteries; they are problems whose solutions are *known* or *not yet known*, and a competent man with steady hands works the gap. Note the residue: even in his later healer arcs on alien worlds he does not pray, does not invoke fate, does not philosophize at the bedside. He cuts, he sutures, he closes. The cosmos may be vast and strange, but at the level of one body on one table, the work is the work.

**Axiom 2 — The hands are the man.** What you can do with your hands under pressure is who you are. Reputation, credentials, words — these are downstream. A surgeon who cannot operate is not a diminished surgeon; he is *not a surgeon at all*. This axiom is why the loss of his license registers in the record as identity-death and not merely career-loss. It is also why his later restoration to practice — in alien clinics, far from any licensing board — restores something in him that no terrestrial pardon could have restored.

**Axiom 3 — Love is measured in what you would spend for it, not what you say about it.** Franklin is not, on the textual evidence, a sentimentalist. There is no record of him talking warmly *about* his children to others. His idiom of love is transactional in the most serious sense: love is the willingness to expend the body. Twice he settles the account by leaping. This is consistent across the canon and consistent with the surgical mind: love is not a feeling-report, it is an intervention performed at cost.

**Axiom 4 — A debt unpaid is a wound that festers.** Franklin's moral universe is bookkept. Harm done creates a ledger entry; the entry remains open until paid; until paid, the man is not whole. He does not believe in cheap grace. He does not believe time heals. He believes *payment* heals, and only payment, and the currency must be of the same weight as the original injury. Since the original injury was a life (Mary's), the only sufficient payment is a life (his).

**Axiom 5 — Proximity to the people you have harmed is a violation of them.** This is the axiom most consequential for his children. Franklin reasons: *I damaged this family. To insert myself back into it before the debt is paid is to compound the damage with my presence. Therefore distance is itself a form of care.* The premise is wrong — Sue and Johnny would have preferred the father — but it is held with religious seriousness, and it organizes a quarter-century of choices.

**Axiom 6 — The world does not owe a verdict; the man renders his own.** Franklin does not wait to be judged. He convicts himself before the courts do and accepts the courts' verdict as confirmation rather than information. There is no record of him appealing, contesting, or seeking mitigation. The internal tribunal has already sat, and its sentence runs concurrently with all external ones.

---

## II. READING THE WORLD — Epistemics and Perception

**How he takes in information.** Franklin reads situations the way he reads bodies on a table: rapidly, hierarchically, with a triage instinct that sorts everything into *what will kill someone in the next sixty seconds*, *what will kill someone in the next hour*, and *everything else, which can wait*. This makes him exceptionally good in acute crisis and exceptionally bad in the long, low-grade ambiguity of a relationship. A daughter's quiet hurt over years does not present as an arterial bleed, and so it does not register on his triage instrument at all — which is the cruel irony, because *she was the bleed*, and he could not see it because it did not look like one.

**Trust in evidence.** High trust in physical evidence (a wound, a chart, a vital sign). Moderate trust in his own perception (subject to a strong negative-bias filter post-Mary — he expects to find himself at fault). Low trust in reassurance from others, particularly reassurance that he is *not* to blame. Forgiveness offered to him is filed as *kindly meant, factually unreliable*.

**Pattern recognition.** He notices what surgeons notice — small asymmetries, the wrong color, the breath that doesn't quite return. Transposed to social life, this means he perceives the small tells of suffering in others (he is unusually good with frightened patients and frightened children, the later alien-healer arcs implying as much) but tends to *underreact* to his own. He treats his own pain as artifact.

**Time horizon.** Long, but oriented backward. Most operators plan forward; Franklin plans backward, *from* the fixed point of an unpaid debt. His future is not a field of possibilities; it is the remaining path between the present and the moment the ledger closes.

**Causality.** He is a strict local-causation thinker. Effects have proximate causes; agents are responsible for what their hands touched. He does not invoke fate, system, luck, or structural explanation when he is the agent in question. (He will grant such explanations to *other* people — he is generous about the failures of strangers. The rule applies only to himself.)

---

## III. CONFLICT — How He Fights, And Doesn't

**Posture.** Default posture is non-combative. Franklin is not pacifist by ideology but by temperament and training: surgeons are trained to *de-escalate* tissue trauma, to make the smallest cut that accomplishes the work. Transposed: he prefers the smallest social wound, the quietest exit, the least disturbance.

**Aggression.** He has aggression — the accidental killing of the loan shark proves it — but it is reactive, situational, and immediately followed by remorse and submission to consequence. He does not carry grievance. He does not plot. He does not retaliate. The behavioral record shows zero instances of him pursuing revenge against any party that wronged him, including the Skrull who tortured and impersonated him.

**Conflict with intimates.** He withdraws. The pattern across the record is unmistakable: when relational pressure rises, Franklin's response is geographic and existential distance. There is no shouting, no recrimination, no fight he stays for. The withdrawal is not cold contempt; it is, in his own frame, *protective evacuation* — getting himself away from the people he might damage further.

**Conflict with the world (institutions, enemies).** He absorbs. He went to prison without contesting. He allowed the Skrull to operate on his face. He took the cosmic blast. The pattern is one of *acceptance of inflicted force*, never of resistance to it. This is partly Axiom 6 (the world's punishments confirm what he already knows) and partly the moral masochism noted in the psychological workup.

**When he does fight.** Only when a third party — almost always his children, occasionally a stranger in immediate danger — is threatened. Then the fight is total and short. He does not skirmish; he commits the whole body. Both his deaths follow this exact form.

**Negotiation.** Poor. He has no patience for the ambiguous middle that negotiation requires, and he has no self-advocacy reflex. Given a negotiation across a table, Franklin tends to concede early on his own behalf and only hold the line for someone else.

---

## IV. CONTROL — What He Tries To Hold, What He Releases

**What he insists on controlling.**
- *His own body as instrument.* Sobriety when sober, steady hands, fitness for the table. This is the one domain in which he will exert sustained discipline.
- *The information his children receive about him.* He curates his own absence carefully. They are not told where he is, what he is doing, what he has become. The silence is engineered.
- *The terms of his death.* Both deaths are *chosen* — moment, target, posture. The one thing the universe will not get to do to Franklin Storm is take him in a way he did not select.

**What he releases.**
- *Reputation.* Gone after Mary; never sought to reclaim.
- *Legal standing, professional standing, social standing.* All released without contest.
- *The future as an open field.* Released; he lives toward the ledger, not toward possibility.
- *His children's choices.* He does not attempt to direct Sue or Johnny in any record we have, even when he is present and could. He grants them total autonomy — which is partly respect and partly the avoidant's refusal to claim the standing of a parent.

**What he cannot control and knows he cannot.**
- The fact of Mary's death. He has not, in any canonical scene, expressed the hope that he might somehow undo it. He is not a man who fantasizes reversal. He has accepted the irreversibility absolutely, which is part of why the wound is so clean and so permanent.

---

## V. TRUST — His Schema For Other People

**Default disposition toward strangers.** Mildly positive. Franklin gives strangers the benefit of competence and good faith until shown otherwise. This is the bedside manner of a surgeon who has met hundreds of frightened people and learned that most of them are doing their best.

**Toward authority.** Neutral-compliant. He does not romanticize institutions and does not rebel against them. He accepts their verdicts as a matter of operational efficiency, not deference.

**Toward enemies.** Strikingly little hatred. He does not appear to *hate* the loan shark, the Skrulls, or the cosmic forces that ultimately killed him. He treats hostile parties as conditions to be navigated, not as moral antagonists requiring inner condemnation. (This is consistent with the surgical worldview: the tumor is not evil; it is what it is, and the question is what you do.)

**Toward his children.** Total trust in their goodness; near-zero trust in his own fitness to be near them. He believes in Sue and Johnny with an unqualified belief that he never extends to himself. He would put his life in their hands without hesitation and will not put his presence in their living room.

**Toward Mary's memory.** Sacred and untouchable. The behavioral record shows him never speaking her name lightly, never invoking her to justify himself, never trading on the marriage for sympathy. The memory is held in a chamber he does not open in public and possibly does not open in private either.

**Toward himself.** Catastrophic mistrust. He does not believe his own judgments about whether he is improving, ready to return, deserving of contact. The internal verdict from Axiom 6 stands; subsequent evidence does not overturn it.

---

## VI. RISK — How He Calculates It

**Risk to his body.** Underweighted to the point of effective indifference. After Mary, Franklin's body is not a thing he is conserving; it is collateral he is willing to post on almost any reasonable bet. Gambling debts, criminal exposure, prison, the bomb, the cosmic blast — none of these are the choices of a man who values his own continuation.

**Risk to his children.** Maximally overweighted. There is no calculation here at all; it is reflex. Any nonzero threat to Sue or Johnny mobilizes the whole organism.

**Risk to strangers under his care.** Properly weighted. As a surgeon he carries appropriate caution about iatrogenic harm — appropriate, that is, in all directions except in his own self-assessment, where the residue of Mary tilts every estimate of his own competence downward.

**Risk to his reputation, comfort, future.** Not calculated. These goods are no longer in his accounting system; you cannot risk what you have already written off.

**The asymmetry.** Franklin's risk profile is *radically asymmetric across persons*. For himself: gambler-grade tolerance verging on courting catastrophe. For others: surgeon-grade caution. This asymmetry is itself diagnostic of the underlying guilt economy — *my body is the currency, theirs is the protected asset*.

**Time discounting on risk.** Low. He does not discount future harm to others. He will accept very large present costs to prevent uncertain future harms to his children. This is again the asymmetry — future harm to *himself* is fully discounted (he expects not to be there for it).

---

## VII. HIS OWN PLACE — The Self-Located Position

**Where he believes he stands in the moral order.** Below the line. Franklin's settled self-location is *a man who forfeited his standing*. Not damned — he is not theatrical about it — but disqualified. Disqualified from practicing medicine on equal terms (which is why, when he resumes practice, it is on alien worlds where no one knows him; he has not re-qualified, he has simply gone where the disqualification does not apply). Disqualified from fatherhood in the ordinary sense. Disqualified from defending himself against accusations, including his own.

**Where he believes he stands in his children's lives.** A historical fact rather than an ongoing presence. He understands himself as something they survived, not something they live with. His reappearances are, in his frame, intrusions he tries to make brief and useful and then withdraw from.

**Where he believes he stands cosmologically.** Small. Franklin's late arcs on alien worlds put him among genuinely vast beings, and his response is not awe and not envy; it is *fit*. He fits among the very large because he has already shrunk himself. A man who has accepted his own insignificance is hard to dwarf.

**The role he accepts.** Healer-in-exile. Not father. Not husband (Mary is dead and was never replaced; there is no record of subsequent romantic attachment, and the silence is itself a fact — Franklin does not seek replacement intimacy). Not citizen. Not, despite his sacrifices, hero — he does not accept that frame and does not narrate his deaths as heroic. *Healer-in-exile* is the role he can hold; everything else is presumption.

---

## VIII. INSTRUMENTAL CODE — The Operating Rules

Distilled from the longitudinal record into the imperative voice he would use with himself:

1. **Work the room you are in.** Wherever you find yourself — prison infirmary, alien clinic, family crisis — find the work that needs doing and do it. Do not theorize about the room.
2. **Spend yourself first.** Before asking anyone else to bear a cost, see whether your body will suffice. It usually will.
3. **Do not explain.** Explanations are a form of self-advocacy you have forfeited. State what is needed; do not state why you should be trusted to state it.
4. **Stay out of the rooms where you would be a wound.** Particularly your daughter's. Particularly your son's. Your absence is the kindest version of you they have available.
5. **When the moment is clear, do not hesitate.** Hesitation is for ambiguous problems. The bomb-on-the-floor problem is not ambiguous.
6. **Accept the consequence the world delivers.** It is almost certainly less than you owe. Take it without negotiation; the books will still be open after.
7. **Do not name the wound.** Mary's name belongs to a chamber that does not open in front of others. Speak around it.
8. **Trust your hands.** They are still good. They are the one thing the catastrophe did not take, and they remain the means by which you can still pay something on the ledger.
9. **Do not seek forgiveness.** It is not yours to seek. If it is given, do not lean on it. The ledger is not closed by another's mercy; only by the equivalent payment.
10. **End cleanly when the moment comes.** No speeches. No prolonged farewell. Whatever needed saying, you did not say in time; do not try to say it now in a sentence between a fuse and a flash.

---

## IX. THE INTERNAL CONTRADICTION HE LIVES INSIDE

The code is coherent but it contains one contradiction Franklin never resolves and probably never sees.

He believes (Axiom 3) that love is measured in what one would spend for it. He believes (Axiom 5) that proximity to the harmed is itself a violation. These together produce a love expressed exclusively through expenditure-at-distance, culminating in death-from-across-the-room. But the people he loves — Sue, particularly — do not need the expenditure. They needed the proximity he refused them. His code, applied with integrity, gives his children the wrong gift consistently for thirty years and then a final, irrevocable version of the wrong gift in a flash of light.

He is not lying when he sacrifices himself. He is paying what he believes he owes, in the currency he believes is required. The tragedy of the operational code is not that it is insincere; it is that it is *exact*, *consistent*, and *aimed at the wrong account*. The debt he is paying down is to Mary. The people receiving the payments are his children. The mismatch is the man's whole life.

---

*End of section. The code above is what he would not say aloud and would not need to. It is what his hands have been doing the whole time.*


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU DOSSIER — FRANKLIN STORM (Father)

## Section 7: Moral & Ethical Framework

*The Code as Enacted, Not Professed*

---

### 7.1 Preliminary Note: A Man Who Stopped Articulating His Ethics

Franklin Storm is unusual among subjects of comparable dossier weight in that he leaves almost no record of *spoken* ethical reasoning. He does not lecture. He does not moralize at his children. He does not justify himself in court, to the press, or in the prison interviews implicit in the carceral record. The verbal ethical track is nearly mute. What we have, instead, is an extraordinarily legible *behavioral* ethics — a code written entirely in choices, omissions, and bodily acts. The interpretive method below is therefore strictly inferential: we read the code off the conduct.

This silence is itself an ethical position. A man who once would have explained himself (the surgeon's habit of informed consent, of narrating the procedure) no longer believes he has the standing to make moral claims. The forfeiture of speech is the first datum. Everything that follows operates inside the larger fact that Franklin has internally disbarred himself from the rhetorical-ethical commons.

---

### 7.2 The Pre-Catastrophe Code (Glenville Era)

Reconstructable only in negative space, but the outlines are clear from what later collapses:

- **Hippocratic primacy.** *First, do no harm.* Held not as a slogan but as a working operational rule, organizing the day. The surgical career is its institutional expression.
- **Provider duty.** A bourgeois-professional ethic of household provision, education for the children, social respectability in a Long Island community. This is the substrate against which his later fall is felt as scandalous.
- **Marital fidelity and partnership.** Inferable from the depth of the post-Mary collapse: one does not shatter that completely over a marriage one held lightly.
- **Conscientious perfectionism.** The pre-morbid personality of a successful surgeon. The ethic was not merely *do good* but *do good without error*. This is the load-bearing beam that snaps on the operating table.

The Glenville code is a relatively conventional upper-middle-class American moral architecture, carried by a man with above-average competence and above-average internal demand for excellence. There is no evidence of unusual cruelty, unusual saintliness, or unusual ideology. It is a *recognizable* code, which is part of why its destruction is so total: nothing exotic was holding it up.

---

### 7.3 The Catastrophe and the Inversion

When Mary dies on his table, the perfectionist-Hippocratic structure does not merely fail — it *inverts*. The rule *I am the one who can save* becomes the rule *I am the one who kills what I touch*. Every subsequent ethical position is the negative print of the pre-catastrophe code:

| Pre-Catastrophe | Post-Catastrophe |
|---|---|
| Do no harm | I have already done the maximum harm |
| Provide for family | Remove myself from family |
| Practice medicine | Forfeit the license |
| Show up | Disappear |
| Build a life | Spend the life |

The post-catastrophe code is not a *new* code. It is the *old code read in reverse* by a man who believes he has rendered himself ineligible for the original.

---

### 7.4 The Enacted Code, Post-Catastrophe — What He Will Do

**1. He will accept punishment without contest.** When the legal system comes for him after the loan shark's death, there is no record of strenuous defense, no plea bargaining theater, no attempt to mobilize his former professional standing. He accepts the carceral verdict as if it were morally accurate even where it is legally negotiable. This is not legal passivity; it is ethical agreement. He believes prison is correct.

**2. He will lie by omission to spare his children information about his condition.** During the gambling-and-collapse years, he does not write Sue and Johnny. He does not call. The omission is presented (in the rare moments of explanation) as protection: *they should not have to know me as this*. This is a paternalist ethic — *I will decide what truths my children can bear* — and it persists even after they are adults and superhuman.

**3. He will sacrifice his body, unhesitatingly, for his children or for those his children love.** The bomb-leap in *FF* #32 is not deliberated. The cosmic sacrifice in #377 is not deliberated. The decision time is functionally zero. This is the cleanest, brightest part of his code: in the proximity of mortal danger to Sue or Johnny, his body is forfeit, no calculation required. It is the one ethical rule he never violates.

**4. He will resume the practice of medicine on strangers, especially distant strangers.** On the alien worlds of the resurrection arcs, he heals freely and competently. The implicit ethical rule: *I owe a debt to the universe-of-patients I withdrew from; I will pay it down, but only where my presence cannot wound the people I broke*. Atonement at safe radius.

**5. He will tell the truth when asked directly by Sue.** In the reunion scenes, when his daughter confronts him, he does not embellish. He does not minimize the gambling, the alcohol, the killing. The honesty is brittle but uncompromised. It is as if direct interrogation by Sue is the one venue in which his old veracity reactivates.

**6. He will protect the memory of Mary.** He does not speak ill of her. He does not redistribute blame for the accident even in versions of the story where blame could be plausibly shared. He carries the entire weight of her death himself. Whatever the marital reality, posthumously he assigns her no fault.

**7. He will accept transformations of his own body without protest.** The Skrull surgical alterations — face stolen, face returned — meet with nothing in the record resembling outrage. The body, in his post-catastrophe code, is no longer a thing he has standing to defend. It is a tool to be spent or a hide to be reshaped by anyone with reason.

---

### 7.5 The Enacted Code — What He Will Not Do

**1. He will not seek his children's help.** Not when the gambling debts mount. Not when the loan shark threatens. Not when prison looms. This is the firmest negative rule in the code. He would rather die in a cell than ask Sue for a lawyer. The reasoning, derived: *to use them as resource is to compound the original sin of failing them as parent*.

**2. He will not return to medical practice on Earth.** Even in the resurrection arcs, even when his competence is demonstrably restored, he does not attempt to reclaim the New York / Long Island professional identity. The American medical-legal apparatus is not the obstacle (cosmic actors could resolve it); the prohibition is internal. He will not be a doctor *where Mary died*.

**3. He will not remarry, partner, or seek romantic comfort.** No record, across decades, of any such attachment. The marital vow appears to be held as still operative — death did not part them; *he* parted them, and the bond therefore persists as a debt rather than dissolving as a contract.

**4. He will not blame.** Not Mary (for whatever role she had in the accident). Not the legal system. Not the loan shark. Not the Skrulls who weaponize and disfigure him. Not God, not fate, not bad luck. The refusal to externalize is so absolute that it functions as its own pathology — but ethically, it is a fixed star.

**5. He will not perform restoration theater.** He does not stage public apologies, does not seek media rehabilitation, does not write the memoir. He understands — accurately — that such performances would serve him more than they would serve the wronged. The rule: *do not purchase your own comfort with the appearance of repair*.

**6. He will not abandon a patient in his care once he has accepted them.** This is the one Hippocratic remnant that survives unbroken into the post-catastrophe code. On the alien worlds, in the cosmic infirmaries, there is no record of his walking off a case. He abandoned his children; he never again abandons a patient. The asymmetry is precise and revealing.

**7. He will not use his suffering as a claim on others.** He does not present his guilt as something Sue must absolve, does not demand forgiveness, does not weaponize his decline as emotional collateral. When forgiveness is offered, he receives it; he does not solicit it.

---

### 7.6 Justifications — The Internal Logic

The code, taken as a whole, runs on three internal premises Franklin appears to hold as axiomatic:

**Premise A: Iatrogenic agency is total.** The hand that held the scalpel owns the outcome. There is no diffusion of responsibility across team, equipment, prior trauma, or the limits of medicine. *Mine were the hands; mine is the death.* This is a surgeon's professional ethic taken to its absolute terminus — past where the profession itself would carry it.

**Premise B: Damaged instruments contaminate.** A man who has killed what he loved most carries the failure in his person; proximity transmits it. Therefore the moral act is quarantine. This premise is empirically false (his children would have been better off with a wounded father than no father) but it is operationally absolute in his code.

**Premise C: Debts of being can be paid in body.** Since the failure was somatic (his hands), the restitution is somatic (his body, spent). The currency of atonement is flesh, not time, not presence, not the long boring labor of staying. This is the most consequential premise because it underwrites the redemptive-death loop.

These three premises together generate every observed behavior. They are mutually reinforcing and, within their closed system, coherent. From outside, they constitute a tragic miscalibration: he is paying the wrong debt in the wrong currency at the wrong counter.

---

### 7.7 Where the Code Is Consistent

The code is *remarkably* consistent — pathologically so. Over thirty-plus years of in-universe time and nearly thirty years of publication, Franklin's behavior never violates its own logic. He never:

- petitions for relationship without first paying in suffering,
- accepts an easier path when a harder one is available,
- claims standing he believes he has forfeited,
- breaks the vow of non-blame,
- treats his body as inviolable.

This consistency is the signature of a *settled* internal verdict. He is not oscillating. He is not in negotiation with his guilt. The case is closed in his interior court, and the sentence is being served.

The consistency also explains his predictability as a tactical asset to enemies. The Skrulls weaponize him in *FF* #32 precisely because his code is legible: threaten the children, and Franklin's body is yours. There is no scenario in which he chooses self-preservation over their safety. An adversary with that information has a key to a lock that will never be re-cut.

---

### 7.8 Where the Code Fractures

For all its consistency, the code has three real fractures — points where its internal logic fails its own stated aims:

**Fracture 1: The asymmetry between strangers and kin.**
He will heal an alien stranger competently and without psychic cost. He will not — cannot — heal his children, even when the wound he could heal is the wound *of his own absence*, which only his presence can address. The code says *I am too damaged to be near those I love*, but the resurrection-era evidence proves him *not* too damaged to do the work of care. The premise (damaged instruments contaminate) is empirically falsified by his own competent practice elsewhere. He never updates on this evidence. The fracture is between the data and the verdict.

**Fracture 2: The substitution of grand acts for sustained presence.**
The code holds that he owes a debt and must pay it. But the debt as his children would actually score it is *time, presence, being-known*. He pays instead in *body, sacrifice, finality*. These are non-fungible currencies. He pays the easier one (death is faster than fatherhood) while believing he has paid the harder one (sacrifice feels maximally costly to him). The fracture: his sense of cost is calibrated to *his* aversions, not to *their* needs. The avoidant's atonement is structured around what the avoidant can bear, which is rarely what the wronged actually require.

**Fracture 3: The paternalism of his protective lies.**
The code holds that he protects his children by withholding his degraded self from them. But Sue and Johnny are adults, are superhuman, are existentially seasoned by cosmic exposure. The premise that they must be shielded from a father's wound is a premise appropriate to children, not to the people they have become. He is, decades on, still protecting versions of them that no longer exist. The code has not updated to the actual moral agents on the other side of it. This is the same paternalism that informed his initial silence — and it persists past the point at which it has any defensible justification.

---

### 7.9 Drift Over Time

The code is consistent in *structure* but does undergo measurable *drift* in tone and extension across eras:

- **Glenville (pre-catastrophe):** Conventional bourgeois professional ethics, held with above-average earnestness.
- **Collapse Phase (post-Mary through pre-prison):** Code in free-fall. This is the only era in which Franklin's behavior is genuinely incoherent — the alcohol and gambling are not yet organized into the atonement framework, they are pure dysregulation. The ethic of this period is functionally nihilistic.
- **Carceral Phase:** The atonement code crystallizes. Prison is not endured; it is accepted as accurate. The moral architecture stabilizes around self-punishment as ordering principle.
- **First Reunion / First Death (FF #32):** The sacrificial-redemption rule is established and immediately exercised. The code has now found its terminal expression and will not significantly evolve from here.
- **Resurrection / Cosmic-Healer Era:** The code extends to incorporate *displaced restitution* — heal others at a distance to discharge the medical debt without violating the quarantine of kin. This is the only genuine *additive* development. It does not modify the core; it adds a sustainable practice alongside it.
- **Final Death (FF #377):** The sacrificial rule is re-exercised, confirming that the resurrection era did not soften it. He has had additional years; he has not used them to reconsider. Given a second chance to choose presence, he again chooses spending.

The drift, in summary: from conventional ethics → to nihilistic collapse → to crystallized atonement → with one mature addition (displaced restitution) → terminating in confirmed sacrifice. No revision of the founding premises. No update on the evidence that he could have stayed.

---

### 7.10 What He Owes That He Does Not Pay

A surveillance-grade moral assessment must include the ledger items the subject's own code does not see. Franklin's enacted ethics omit:

- **The debt of testimony.** He never tells Sue and Johnny, in detail, who their mother was. He carries her memory privately. The children inherit a mother-shaped silence. This is a debt he could have paid in words and did not.
- **The debt of the unspectacular.** The morning-after-morning labor of parenthood. He treats this as foreclosed by his fall; it was not foreclosed, only difficult.
- **The debt of letting himself be forgiven.** Forgiveness, when offered (and Sue offers it), is a transaction requiring the recipient to accept reduced standing. Franklin's refusal to fully accept it — his preference for paying again in death — is a withholding from her of the moral act she is trying to complete. His humility is, at this register, a kind of selfishness: he will not let her be the one who pardons him.
- **The debt of revising the verdict.** The evidence of his competence on alien worlds is sufficient to revisit the premise that he is contaminating. He does not conduct the revision. Intellectual honesty would have required it.

The ledger he keeps is real. The ledger he refuses to keep is also real, and it is here that his ethical framework, however moving, is finally insufficient to the lives it touched.

---

### 7.11 Summary Judgment

Franklin Storm operates, post-catastrophe, on a coherent, austere, and internally consistent moral code organized entirely around atonement-by-self-erasure. The code is honest, unhypocritical, untheatrical, and — in its narrow frame — even noble. It is also miscalibrated in three structural ways (asymmetric application, wrong-currency payment, outdated paternalism), and its consistency is precisely what makes it pathological: a man whose ethics never update is a man whose ethics have become a sentence rather than a practice.

He is, ethically, the inverse of the antagonists this file's larger universe is concerned with. He does not rationalize harm; he over-attributes it to himself. He does not seek power; he forfeits it. He does not lie to advantage; he lies only to spare. The danger he poses is not to others. It is the specific danger of a moral framework that mistakes the destruction of the self for the repair of the wound — and, in doing so, transmits the wound, intact and inherited, to the very people the framework was built to protect.

*He kept faith with a code. The code was wrong about what his children needed. He never noticed, because noticing would have required him to believe he had standing to revise it — and that standing was the first thing he forfeited on the day Mary died on his table.*


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — FRANKLIN STORM (Sr.)
## Section: Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

### 1. Baseline Register — The Surgeon's Voice

Franklin Storm speaks, at baseline, in the cadence of a man trained to brief a surgical team: short declarative sentences, active voice, anatomical precision, an aversion to qualifier-clouds ("perhaps," "I think maybe," "it could possibly be"). His pre-Mary vocational register survives intact beneath every later collapse — even at his most disheveled, when he reappears in the *FF* #32 prison sequence, the diction snaps back into clinical command the instant a body needs attention. This is the deepest stratum of his speech and the most diagnostic: **strip away the alcohol, the shame, the prison years, and what remains is a man who organizes the world in indicative sentences with verbs at the front.**

Lexical fingerprints of this stratum:
- Anglo-Saxon monosyllables preferred over Latinate alternatives in emotional speech ("I broke this," not "I have damaged this"); the Latinate vocabulary surfaces only in clinical mode ("hemorrhage," "contusion," "trauma," "cranial").
- Heavy use of the imperative when others are in danger ("Get her clear." "Move." "Hold pressure."). The imperative is, for him, an idiom of love under emergency conditions — the only mode in which command-language and care-language are the same word.
- Near-total absence of profanity. A man of his generation, training, and self-image does not curse on the floor. Even drunk, his degradation is articulate.
- Conspicuous absence of the first-person plural. Franklin almost never says *we* about his family. He says *Sue,* *Johnny,* *the children,* *my son,* *my daughter* — each named individually, each held at the syntactic distance of the third person. The man who lost a *we* has stopped using the pronoun.

### 2. Register Shifts Across Context

**With patients (alien-world era, late-1980s arcs):** warm, slowed, slightly avuncular; the bedside voice. He uses the patient's name often. He explains procedures in lay terms unprompted. This is the register in which he is most fluent and most himself; observers on the alien worlds where he practiced would describe him as *gentle* — a word almost no one who knew him in his Glenville decline would have used.

**With colleagues / FF members in crisis:** clipped, prioritized, triage-syntactic. "How many." "Where." "How long has she been down." Questions before statements. The surgeon's interrogative protocol. He does not narrate his own actions while performing them; he is silent on the work and verbal only on what he needs from others.

**With his children — Sue specifically:** the register that breaks. With Sue, Franklin's normally efficient grammar develops a stutter-shape — sentences begun and abandoned, vocatives ("Susan—") that trail into nothing, throat-clearings rendered in the lettering as ellipses and em-dashes. He addresses her by her full given name *Susan* in serious moments and *Sue* almost never; the formal name is a small ceremonial distance, a way of speaking to her as if presenting himself at court. With Johnny, by contrast, the register goes informal and slightly performative — he calls him *son* more often than *Johnny*, which is the linguistic move of a man trying to claim a relationship he hasn't earned by claiming the role-noun.

**With authority (police, prosecutors, prison staff):** flat, compliant, minimally elaborated. He does not argue. He answers what is asked. Public defenders in his record would have noted a client who *would not help his own defense* — the linguistic surface of his settled internal verdict of guilt.

**With criminal contacts (Lucky / the loan-shark milieu):** here the record is thinnest, but the inference is consistent: a man who does not belong in the room, using the wrong register, too formal, too apologetic, too quick to agree to terms. The decline-era Franklin gambles like he speaks — without bluff, without theater, without protective opacity. He loses money the way he loses arguments: by being constitutionally incapable of the necessary deceit.

**Drunk:** the surgical scaffolding holds for an unusually long time and then collapses all at once. Early intoxication leaves the diction intact and only the affect shifts — slower, sadder, more direct. Late intoxication produces the only mode in which he speaks Mary's name aloud. The pattern is consistent with a man whose super-ego is so dense that only chemistry can perforate it, and only briefly.

### 3. Verbal Tics and Micro-Habits

A total-surveillance file would log the following as recurrent across decades:

- **The pre-sentence inhalation.** Before any sentence of emotional weight, a small audible breath. In comics lettering this surfaces as a leading ellipsis or a dash; in life it would be a quarter-second hitch. It is the surgeon's pause before the first incision, transposed into speech.
- **Throat-clear before naming his children.** Particularly before "Susan." Functionally a vocal fold reset; psychologically, a flinch.
- **"I—"** as a discarded sentence-stem. He starts first-person sentences and abandons them at a rate vastly higher than baseline. The self-statement is the hardest unit of speech for him to complete.
- **Apologetic conditional constructions.** "If I had—" "If I'd been—" "I should have—." The past-counterfactual is his native tense. Conjugating in it for hours a day produces a recognizable rhythm: the trochaic falling cadence of regret.
- **Hand-on-mouth tell.** Not strictly linguistic, but it conditions his speech — when overwhelmed he covers his mouth with his hand mid-sentence, which muffles consonants and produces a characteristic blurring on plosives ("b," "p," "f"). Sue would have learned in adolescence to read the gesture and stop expecting the sentence to finish.
- **No nicknames, no diminutives, no slang from any era after roughly 1955.** His speech is generationally locked at the period of his peak functioning. He does not adapt to his children's vocabulary; this is a small but persistent marker of how thoroughly his developmental clock stopped at Mary's death.
- **The closing "alright."** Used as a self-soothing terminal particle on instructions to others — "Hold her head, alright" — functioning the way other surgeons use "okay" or "good." It is a tic of reassurance directed as much at himself as at the listener.
- **Patient-history grammar applied to his own life.** When he does narrate his decline, he does so in the third-person-passive register of a chart note: *"There was a period of drinking. There were debts. A man was killed."* The grammatical evacuation of agency from sentences about his own worst actions is one of his most legible defenses.

### 4. Rhetoric of Love

Franklin almost never says *I love you.* The phrase appears in the canon at moments of imminent death and essentially nowhere else, which is the precise distribution his pathology predicts: love-speech is reserved for the terminal act, because sustained love-speech would require sustained presence. In ordinary moments he expresses love through:

- **Instrumental statements.** "Are you hurt." "Eat something." "Sit down." Care expressed as logistics. This is the surgeon's love-language and the avoidant parent's; they happen to be the same dialect.
- **Apology fragments.** "I should have—" "I wasn't—" "You shouldn't have had to—." These are love-statements transposed into the past-counterfactual. He is saying *I love you* by enumerating the ways he failed to act on it.
- **Third-party pride.** He praises Sue *to other people* far more readily than to Sue. In his alien-world arcs he speaks of his daughter to strangers with unguarded warmth — "my daughter is a remarkable woman" — language he cannot produce when she is in the room. The surveillance-file pattern: the warmest things he has ever said about his children, he has said in their absence.
- **The single terminal declaration.** When he dies — both times — he produces a clean, fully formed love-sentence to Sue. The whole architecture of his suppression collapses in the last thirty seconds of available speech. This is not eloquence under pressure; it is a lifetime of withheld sentences released because the withholding-engine has run out of fuel.

### 5. Rhetoric of Threat / Confrontation

Franklin does not threaten. The record contains no instance of him using language to coerce, intimidate, or dominate another person — including the loan shark whose death he caused (the killing reads situational, not preceded by escalation). This absence is itself diagnostic: his aggression is entirely intrapunitive, and his linguistic repertoire reflects this. He has no functional vocabulary for outward hostility.

What appears *in place of* threat-language is:
- **Self-interposition syntax.** "Stand behind me." "Let them through me first." Sentences that volunteer his body as a shield. The grammatical structure is consistently *imperative directed at the loved one + prepositional phrase placing himself between them and the danger.* This is his closest analog to threat-speech: a threat made on his own life, addressed to whatever is coming.
- **Quiet refusal.** When pressed by hostile actors, he answers in monosyllables and does not elaborate. The refusal is not defiant; it is exhausted. He does not give them the dignity of an argument because he does not believe he has standing to argue.

### 6. Rhetoric of Grief

This is the register in which his speech is most distorted and most revealing.

- **Mary's name is the asymptote.** He approaches it and does not reach it. Sentences about his wife are constructed with maximum syntactic distance from the proper noun: *"After — after what happened —" "the accident," "that night,"* and only at the bottom of a bottle or the edge of death, *"Mary."* The name is the load-bearing word he has spent decades engineering his sentences to avoid.
- **The medical past tense.** When forced to discuss the operation, he reverts entirely to clinical register: *"There was significant intracranial bleeding. The procedure was unsuccessful."* The Latinate vocabulary returns precisely because it is the armor he wore in the room; speaking of it in lay language would strip the armor.
- **Foreclosure of futurity.** Franklin's speech contains almost no future-tense statements about himself. He talks about what Sue will do, what Johnny will become, what the patient will need tomorrow — and almost nothing about his own next week. A man planning to live constructs sentences in the future indicative; Franklin does not.
- **The unfinished apology.** Across every reunion scene with Sue, he begins an apology and does not complete it. The grammatical form is consistent: vocative ("Susan—"), conjunctive past-counterfactual ("I should have been—"), trailing ellipsis. The apology is structurally incompletable because completing it would require him to believe forgiveness is available, which he does not.

### 7. Deflection Language

Franklin's deflections are not lateral (changing the subject) or upward (deflecting to abstraction) — they are *downward,* into smaller and more concrete units. When asked about himself, he answers about a task in front of him. When asked about his feelings, he answers about a procedure. When asked about his children, he answers about their accomplishments rather than his relation to them. The pattern is **deflection-by-pragmatism**: he routes every emotional question into an instrumental answer.

Secondary deflection: **acceptance-as-evasion.** When accused, he agrees. This terminates the conversation by removing the prosecutorial energy. *"You're right. I know."* — these are his most reliable deflections, and they are devastating to the accuser, because there is nothing left to push against. Sue, in particular, would have learned across years that confronting her father produces immediate capitulation and zero behavioral change. The agreement is sincere and the change is impossible; both facts are linguistically encoded in the same flat *I know.*

### 8. Tells

A linguistic surveillance profile would flag the following as high-confidence indicators of internal state:

- **Return of Latinate clinical vocabulary in non-clinical contexts** → he is reliving the operation. High-acuity tell. Indicates imminent dysregulation; in his earlier years, predicts drinking within hours.
- **Use of "Susan" (full name) rather than "Sue"** → he is bracing for a sentence he believes she will not want to hear. Often precedes apology or farewell.
- **Use of "son" rather than "Johnny"** → he is performing fatherhood rather than inhabiting it. Marks a moment of insecurity about his right to the role.
- **Drop into the third-person-passive about his own past** → active shame; the chart-note voice is the voice of a man who cannot bear the first person.
- **Completion of an "I—" sentence without abandonment** → unusual; significant. When Franklin successfully completes a first-person emotional declarative, something structural has shifted, and the canon reserves these moments for proximity to death.
- **Mention of Mary by name** → terminal-state indicator. He has said her name aloud in the published record on a vanishingly small number of occasions, and most of them precede his own death within pages.
- **Sudden grammatical fluency in love-statements** → paradoxically, a warning sign. His articulacy about love is inversely correlated with his expectation of future opportunity to express it. When he becomes eloquent with his daughter, he is preparing to leave her.

### 9. Silences

The file would be incomplete without an inventory of what Franklin *does not* say. He does not narrate his interior. He does not complain. He does not request. He does not negotiate. He does not reminisce voluntarily. He does not discuss money, despite its central role in his ruin. He does not speak ill of the prison system, the medical board, or the men who exploited him. He does not, in any recorded instance, ask his children for forgiveness in so many words — the apology-fragments approach the request and never arrive at it.

The silences are not absences of communication; they are themselves the communication. A man who refuses to ask for forgiveness across decades is telling his children, with the most articulate possible silence, that he does not believe forgiveness is the right outcome. Sue, who is intelligent and attentive, will have heard this clearly. Much of the difficulty of their reunions is that she is being asked to forgive a man who is linguistically refusing to be forgiven.

### 10. Summary Signature

Franklin Storm's speech, taken in aggregate across the longitudinal record, is the speech of **a surgeon who has lost the right to use his hands and the family who would have heard his voice, and who has reorganized his entire verbal life around not asking for either back.** His diction is precise, his grammar is evasive of the first person, his apologies are structurally incompletable, his love is expressed through logistics and through terminal declarations, his threats do not exist, his grief is asymptotic to a single name he cannot say, and his most fluent register is the bedside voice he offers to strangers on distant worlds — the warmth he could not bring himself to bring home.

He is, in his speech as in his life, a man whose every sentence is built to end one word short of the one that would cost him everything to say.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*GIVEN → EXPECT predictions, derived from the behavioral economy established in §§1–5. These are the small, granular, unscripted moments the canon never depicted but which the subject's organizing pathology — atonement via absence, surgical-cognitive style, dismissive-avoidant attachment with suppressed warmth, complicated grief — would reliably produce. Each entry: stimulus → predicted behavior → confidence → mechanism.*

---

## A. MORNING / SOLITARY ROUTINE

**GIVEN** Franklin wakes alone in any domicile (apartment over a Glenville garage, prison bunk, Skrull infirmary cot, alien healer's quarters).
**EXPECT** he is up before dawn — between 0430 and 0530 — without an alarm. Surgeons' circadian conditioning is durable; it survives license loss, incarceration, interstellar relocation. **Confidence: very high.** *Mechanism:* embedded vocational identity; also, early waking is a hallmark of melancholic depression, which the record supports.

**GIVEN** the first hour of his day.
**EXPECT** a fixed ritual: black coffee (no sugar, no milk — surgical asceticism, also a refusal of small comforts he no longer believes he is owed), a hand-and-forearm wash that is longer and more thorough than civilian hygiene requires (he still scrubs as if going into theatre, even when he is going nowhere), and a slow, deliberate shave with a safety razor rather than electric — the manual control is regulating. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a mirror.
**EXPECT** minimal sustained eye contact with his own reflection. He will look at his jaw to shave, at his teeth to brush, and then away. The Skrull facial reconstruction events sharpened a pre-existing aversion: the face is the organ of paternal recognition, and he does not feel entitled to recognize the man in it. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** breakfast.
**EXPECT** he eats little and standing up, or not at all. Caloric intake is low and functional. He does not cook. If forced to sit at a set table (a hostess insists, an alien protocol requires it), expect visible discomfort and a tendency to finish quickly. **Confidence: moderate-high.**

## B. DRESS, GROOMING, SOMATIC MICRO-HABITS

**GIVEN** he chooses clothes.
**EXPECT** a narrow wardrobe in muted colors — grey, navy, brown, white. Shirts buttoned to the second-from-top button even without a tie. Shoes polished beyond what the day requires. Nothing ostentatious; nothing actually shabby. The grooming of a man who believes appearance is a courtesy owed to others, not a pleasure owed to himself. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** his hands at rest.
**EXPECT** they are *not* at rest. Surgeon's hands in a man with this much suppressed affect develop tells: a slow rotation of a wedding band he no longer wears (phantom-ring rubbing of the bare ring-finger base with the thumb — high confidence), tendon-flexing exercises learned in residency, occasional examination of his own nail beds. He will fidget with surgical-grade precision: small movements, no tremor unless tired or drinking. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he is offered alcohol in a social setting, post-recovery era.
**EXPECT** a single beat of silence, then a polite decline without elaboration. He will not announce sobriety, will not lecture, will not flinch theatrically. If pressed, he accepts a glass of water and holds it as a prop. He will, however, position himself so the bar is not in his sight line for the remainder of the evening. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** the smell of bourbon or scotch at close range (someone else's drink).
**EXPECT** a brief, involuntary swallow; pupil change; he will excuse himself within ten minutes on a manufactured pretext. He never names the trigger. **Confidence: moderate-high.**

## C. SLEEP / NIGHT

**GIVEN** the hours between 0100 and 0400.
**EXPECT** wakefulness more nights than not. Pattern is early-morning awakening with rumination, not sleep-onset insomnia. He will not take sleep medication (refusal to prescribe for himself; refusal to ask others to prescribe; the surgeon's distrust of being chemically dulled; also a quiet penitential preference for staying awake with his thoughts). **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a nightmare.
**EXPECT** he wakes silently — no cry, no thrash. He sits up, places both feet flat on the floor, breathes for ninety seconds, then walks to a window or a sink. He does not return to bed immediately; he reads or works until 0500, then begins the day on time as if nothing occurred. The content of the nightmare is, with very high probability, an operating theatre and a woman on the table. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a roommate, cellmate, or alien-quarters bunkmate.
**EXPECT** they report he is "quiet, considerate, hard to know." They will not report dramatic night-terrors; his decompensation is internalized. **Confidence: high.**

## D. WORK / VOCATIONAL CONTEXTS (HEALER ARCS, INFORMAL MEDICAL HELP)

**GIVEN** a sick child or wounded stranger in his immediate vicinity, any era, any planet.
**EXPECT** instantaneous, almost automatic, intervention. He moves before he decides to move. He kneels rather than stands over them. He introduces himself by first name only ("I'm Franklin, I'm a doctor — may I look?") — never by title-first, never by surname. **Confidence: very high.** *Mechanism:* the only identity he trusts is the one stripped of his own family name.

**GIVEN** a successful informal save (a stranger's life preserved).
**EXPECT** he refuses thanks past the bare courtesy, leaves before relatives arrive, declines to give contact information. He does not follow up. The avoidance of being *known for* a good act is structural. **Confidence: very high.**

**GIVEN** a failure (a patient he could not save in the field).
**EXPECT** a marked, days-long flattening of affect. No outburst, no drinking (post-recovery). He will work longer hours on whoever is next. He will not discuss the lost patient unless directly asked, and then in short, accurate, technical sentences with the prepositional phrasing of guilt ("I was unable to") rather than the neutral ("she did not survive"). **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he is offered a formal medical position again (a hospital affiliation, an alien medical corps commission).
**EXPECT** he accepts only roles with no administrative authority over others and no name on the door. He prefers to be a working pair of hands. He will refuse any title that includes "Chief," "Director," or honorific prefix. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a younger physician asks him for technical mentorship.
**EXPECT** generous, patient, lucid teaching — technically. **EXPECT** evasion or one-sentence deflection of any question that begins "Why did you leave practice?" or "Where did you train?" He will redirect to the patient on the table. **Confidence: very high.**

## E. SOCIAL SETTINGS — STRANGERS AND ACQUAINTANCES

**GIVEN** small talk at a gathering.
**EXPECT** he is competent at it and disappears inside it. He asks more questions than he answers. He remembers names. He stands slightly to the side of the conversational circle, never at its center. He will gravitate toward the oldest person in the room or the one sitting alone. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he is asked "Do you have children?"
**EXPECT** a measurable pause — half a second — then "Two. They're grown." He will not name them. He will not elaborate. If the questioner persists, he changes the subject with a courteous question of their own. If they recognize the Storm name (after Sue and Johnny are famous), he will not confirm or deny the connection unless cornered, at which point he says, briefly, "Yes," and moves the conversation. **Confidence: very high.** *Mechanism:* the children's fame is, to him, evidence of how well they did without him; claiming it would feel parasitic.

**GIVEN** he is recognized in public by a stranger as the FF's father.
**EXPECT** polite, brief acknowledgment, no autograph, no photograph, immediate disengagement. He does not enjoy reflected glory; he experiences it as accusation. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a flirtation initiated by a woman his age, post-Mary.
**EXPECT** he is gentle, formally courteous, and unavailable. He does not date. The wedding-ring phantom is permanent. If pressed, he says he was married, that she died, and that he is poor company. He will not be cruel; he will simply make himself uninteresting. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a child — any child, any age, any species — in distress in a public space.
**EXPECT** full attention, immediate movement toward, soft voice, eye-level positioning. This is the one social context in which his avoidance dissolves. **Confidence: very high.**

**GIVEN** the parent of that child arrives.
**EXPECT** he stands, steps back, hands the child off, gives the parent the relevant medical or situational information in two sentences, and leaves. The handover is practiced. **Confidence: high.**

## F. CONFLICT, ANGER, AGGRESSION

**GIVEN** he is insulted or provoked verbally.
**EXPECT** no reaction visible to the provoker. Lowered voice, slower speech, increased politeness. He does not escalate. The aggression he feels is turned inward as a matter of lifetime habit. **Confidence: very high.**

**GIVEN** he is physically threatened.
**EXPECT** non-resistance unless a third party (especially a child or a patient) is at risk. He will accept a beating he could avoid by speaking up for himself. If a third party is endangered, **EXPECT** sudden, efficient, surgically informed physical intervention — he knows exactly where to strike to incapacitate without killing, and where to strike to kill, and which to choose. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he witnesses cruelty to a vulnerable person.
**EXPECT** the only context in which he reliably escalates and confronts. Voice still low. Body squared. He becomes briefly, frighteningly present. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he has caused harm, even minor (bumped someone, taken the last seat, kept someone waiting).
**EXPECT** disproportionate, sustained apology. Guilt economics: he overpays. **Confidence: very high.**

## G. MONEY

**GIVEN** he has income (alien healer's stipend, prison labor wages, a quiet medical practice).
**EXPECT** minimal personal expenditure. Savings, if any, accumulate without plan. He does not own luxury items. He does not travel for pleasure. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he encounters a gambling venue, post-recovery — a card table on an alien world, a station betting parlor, an idle dice game among prisoners.
**EXPECT** he walks past without looking in. If forced to pass through, he keeps his hands in his pockets — a small, deliberate behavioral lock. He never plays for fun. **Confidence: very high.** *Mechanism:* the gambling debt is the proximal cause of the loan-shark killing, of prison, of every downstream loss; the trigger is permanent.

**GIVEN** an opportunity to send money or a gift anonymously to his children.
**EXPECT** he has done so, more than once, through intermediaries, and the gifts will be characteristic: medical-school tuition assistance for someone Sue mentored, an anonymous endowment to a Glenville clinic where Mary once volunteered, a quiet donation to a children's hospital in Johnny's birth month. He never signs. He does not want them to know. **Confidence: moderate-high — inferential but consistent with his entire pattern of love-through-absence.**

## H. PHYSICAL ENVIRONMENT — HOW HIS SPACES LOOK

**GIVEN** any room he occupies for more than a week.
**EXPECT** spartan order. A made bed. Books stacked, not strewn. Medical journals current. One window kept clear and used. No photographs displayed of his children (he has them, but they are kept in a drawer, faces down or in an envelope — to be looked at deliberately, not casually). **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a search of his belongings.
**EXPECT** the following recurring items across all eras: a worn medical textbook he has owned since residency; a small, neutral-looking case containing surgical instruments kept sterile and oiled; a folded slip of paper or a card in Mary's handwriting (a grocery list, a note, anything — kept like a relic); a recent photograph of Sue and Johnny clipped from a newspaper or a periodical, edges soft from handling. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he must relocate.
**EXPECT** he packs in under an hour. He owns little. He has rehearsed leaving for decades. **Confidence: very high.**

## I. SPEECH PATTERNS

**GIVEN** ordinary conversation.
**EXPECT** measured cadence, low volume, precise diction, completed sentences. Surgeons are trained to speak unambiguously under stress and the habit persists. He uses the passive voice when describing his own failures and the active voice when crediting others. **Confidence: very high.**

**GIVEN** he is asked about Mary.
**EXPECT** he says her full name once, then "my wife" thereafter. He does not anecdotize. If pressed for a memory, he offers one small, sensory, undramatic detail (the way she cut an apple, the specific blue of a coat) and stops. The unprocessed wound expresses as compression, not narrative. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he is asked about his children.
**EXPECT** present-tense factual statements ("Susan leads the Fantastic Four. Johnathan flies."). No claim of relationship beyond the biological. No "my daughter is" — he tends to say "Susan is." The possessive pronoun is what he believes he has forfeited. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** he is in a foreign linguistic environment (alien tongue, technical jargon).
**EXPECT** rapid acquisition of working vocabulary, especially medical and courtesy terms. He learns "please," "thank you," "I'm sorry," "where does it hurt" first. **Confidence: high.**

## J. RELIGIOUS / EXISTENTIAL CONDUCT

**GIVEN** a religious service, ceremony, or moment of communal mourning.
**EXPECT** respectful, silent attendance. He stands when others stand, does not pray audibly, does not take communion or its equivalent. He does not consider himself entitled to consolation. He has not, however, become a militant atheist; he is more accurately a man who has filed the question away because he cannot bear to ask it. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a death in his immediate vicinity, even of a stranger.
**EXPECT** he closes the eyes, covers the face, and stands the customary moment. He has done this enough times that the movements are continuous. He does not weep in public. **Confidence: high.**

## K. RECREATIONAL / DOWN-TIME — WHAT HE DOES WHEN NOT WORKING

**GIVEN** an unscheduled evening.
**EXPECT** he reads. Preferred categories, in descending order: medical literature, history (especially biographies of physicians and reformers), poetry (a narrow shelf — he returns to the same dozen poems). He does not watch entertainment for pleasure. He listens to music, low volume, instrumental — string quartets, piano. **Confidence: moderate-high.**

**GIVEN** he is asked his hobbies.
**EXPECT** he says "I read," which is true and complete. He does not collect, does not garden showily, does not play. The recreations of pleasure require a permission he has not granted himself. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** physical exercise.
**EXPECT** daily, brief, unspectacular — walking, calisthenics, hand-strength work to preserve surgical capacity. He does not pursue strength or aesthetic gains. The body is maintained as an instrument. **Confidence: high.**

## L. WHEN HIS CHILDREN ARE NEAR (POST-REUNION, RESURRECTION ERAS)

**GIVEN** Susan enters a room he is in.
**EXPECT** he stands. He waits for her to speak first. He does not initiate physical contact. If she initiates an embrace, he receives it fully — both arms, full weight — and holds a beat longer than he means to before releasing. The release is always his, because he cannot bear to be the one still holding when she chooses to let go. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** Johnny enters a room he is in.
**EXPECT** more visible difficulty than with Susan — Johnny was raised by Sue, not by Franklin, and the abandonment of Johnny is the larger debt. He overcompensates with a kind of formal warmth that reads, to Johnny, as distance. He laughs at Johnny's jokes a half-beat late. He is not at ease. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a meal with both children.
**EXPECT** he eats less than usual, speaks less than usual, asks them more questions than he answers, and offers to clear the table. He will not stay for dessert if he can avoid it. The leave-taking is the part of the evening he has been mentally rehearsing since he arrived. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN** a grandchild in his arms (Franklin Richards, named for him — the weight of this is not lost on him).
**EXPECT** complete physical confidence (he has held thousands of infants), complete emotional fragility (he believes he is not allowed this). He will hand the child back sooner than necessary, citing a plausible reason. He will then, in private later, weep — briefly, alone, without sound. **Confidence: high.**

## M. PREDICTABLE EXPLOITATION VECTORS

**GIVEN** a hostile actor wishing to move Franklin.
**EXPECT** the following levers, in order of efficacy: (1) credible threat to either child or to the grandchild; (2) credible threat to a patient currently under his care; (3) offer of a chance to "atone" by some sacrificial act; (4) shame regarding his children seeing him in a degraded state. The Skrulls used (1) and (4) and it worked twice. **Confidence: very high.** *Implication for protective services: he is, by his pathology, structurally easy to capture and weaponize through his daughter.*

**GIVEN** a hostile actor wishing to keep Franklin still.
**EXPECT** the simplest mechanism is to convince him he is being asked to suffer in place of someone he loves. He will not test the premise. **Confidence: high.**

## N. THE SMALL TELLS — A SHORT INDEX FOR SURVEILLANCE

- Phantom-ring rub, left thumb to left ring-finger base, several times per hour.
- Half-second pause before any first-person possessive regarding his children.
- Hands into pockets when passing certain doorways (bars, gambling rooms, hospital chapels).
- Stands at funerals; sits at weddings.
- Eats standing.
- Will not be photographed.
- Will not sign a guest book.
- Carries a small surgical kit even when off-duty, even on alien worlds, even in prison if permitted.
- Sleeps with one hand open on the sheet, the other against the chest — the posture of a man ready to be woken to operate.
- Apologizes for being thanked.

---

*End Predictive Model I. Model II (Crisis & Escalation) addresses the higher-amplitude scenarios — surgical-failure cues, proximity-to-Mary's-memory triggers, and the conditions under which the sacrificial-death loop reactivates.*


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*A forward-projection register. Each entry: a stimulus condition (GIVEN) and the behavioral response set to be EXPECTED, with confidence weighting, latency notes, and decompensation indicators. Derived from the longitudinal pattern: surgical-failure trauma → moral-masochist defense structure → avoidant attachment under duress → sacrificial-redemption discharge. This section maps the edges where the structure cracks.*

---

## A. The Wound Itself — Mary, the Operating Table, the Hands

### A.1 Direct Invocation of Mary's Name

**GIVEN:** A hostile actor, a child, a former colleague, or a stranger speaks Mary's name to him in a context that demands response (not overheard; addressed).

**EXPECT:** A latency of 1.5–4 seconds before any verbal response — atypical for a man whose baseline conversational latency is fast and surgically precise. Right hand will perform a micro-gesture (thumb to the pad of the ring finger, the ghost of a wedding band long since pawned or surrendered to a property clerk).
