- **A third sacrificial death, or a functional equivalent.** Statistically, this is the most likely terminus. The subject has a two-for-two record of resolving the unbearable proximity of his children by interposing his body between them and a threat. The third instance, if permitted, will be narratively framed as redemption and will in fact be the final, most consummate refusal of fatherhood.

This base-rate forecast is not pessimism. It is the straight-line extrapolation of a man who has, across sixty years of published existence, never once chosen the slower, less photogenic option.

---

### 2. The Fork Points

There are, by my count, **five identifiable fork points** in the subject's likely forward path. Each is a moment where a small choice produces a large divergence in long-run outcome.

#### Fork 1 — The First Conversation About Mary

At some point, somebody — most plausibly Sue, possibly a grandchild who has no investment in the old silence — will ask Franklin to talk about Mary. Not about the accident. About *her*. Her laugh, her habits, what she cooked, what she fought with him about.

- **Growth limb:** He talks. He is bad at it at first, clipped and surgical, then gradually less so. The talking does what talking does — it converts a frozen catastrophe into a narrative with a beginning, a middle, and survivors. This is the single highest-leverage intervention available on the subject. It is also the one he will most strenuously avoid.
- **Catastrophe limb:** He deflects with a self-deprecating remark, changes the subject to the present crisis, or — most likely — physically leaves the room on a pretext ("I should check on…"). The opportunity does not re-present itself for years, if ever. The wound calcifies further.

The fork is decided in roughly ninety seconds of real time, on a couch or in a kitchen, with no superhuman element present. It is the most important ninety seconds of his remaining life.

#### Fork 2 — The Grandchildren

Franklin's existing grandchildren — and any subsequent — present him with an opportunity his children could not: people he did not fail in the original injury. They carry no firsthand grievance. They will, if permitted, simply like him.

- **Growth limb:** He allows himself to be *ordinarily* loved by someone — to be Grandpa, to be asked to fix a toy, to be told a secret, to be drawn in crayon. The accumulating low-stakes intimacy gradually rewires his attachment system. The grandchildren become the safe ground on which he eventually learns to stand in front of his own children.
- **Catastrophe limb:** He keeps them at the same arm's length he keeps his children at, on the rationalized ground that he is "not safe for them" — projecting his self-verdict forward another generation. He sends gifts from off-world. He shows up for the heroic moments and absents himself from the birthdays. He reproduces the pattern at one further remove.

The subject's surgical-displacement defense will incline him strongly toward the catastrophe limb. The grandchildren themselves are the most plausible disruptor, because young children do not respect the geometry of an adult's avoidance.

#### Fork 3 — Reclamation of the License / Domestic Practice

Symbolically and practically, the question of whether Franklin practices medicine *on Earth, under his own name, in a building his children could visit* is the question of whether he is willing to be ordinarily present.

- **Growth limb:** He pursues reinstatement. He works in a clinic in Glenville, or Brooklyn, or somewhere humbler. He becomes locatable. He has a phone number Sue can call. The mundanity of this is precisely its therapeutic content: a man with a phone number is a man who can be a father.
- **Catastrophe limb:** He continues to practice only at cosmic remove — the alien colony, the dimensional outpost, the emergency intervention — where the work is real but the address is unreachable. He remains a healer whose patients are always strangers and whose family must travel light-years to be in the same room with him.

This fork is the one most likely to be miscoded as a logistical question ("where's the work?") when it is in fact an identity question ("am I a man who can be reached?").

#### Fork 4 — The Next Sacrificial Moment

There will be another moment in which Franklin can interpose his body. The subject's response in that instant is the most legible single test of trajectory.

- **Growth limb:** He acts to save, but he does not seek to die. He uses his competence — surgical, tactical, relational — to produce an outcome in which everyone, including himself, survives. He returns home that night. He has dinner. He has, for the first time in his adult life, refused the seductive solution of redemptive self-erasure.
- **Catastrophe limb:** He takes the bomb again, in some new aesthetic. He dies a third time, beautifully. His children weep at another funeral. The pattern is sealed and the trajectory is over.

It is essential to understand that the *catastrophe limb here will feel, to the subject in the moment, like virtue*. It will be experienced as love. This is what makes it so difficult to interrupt. Any prophylactic intervention must occur long before the moment itself — must consist of having previously convinced him, somewhere in his slow internal weather, that *staying alive for his children is a harder and truer gift than dying for them*. This is the single most important sentence in his treatment, and he has not yet heard it from a source he believes.

#### Fork 5 — Aging Into Ordinary Mortality

If — and this is the lowest-probability but highest-value branch — Franklin survives long enough to face *non-heroic* mortality, he encounters a problem his entire defensive architecture is unequipped for: a death that cannot be converted into a sacrifice. Cardiac event. Cancer. The slow erosions of a body in its seventies and eighties.

- **Growth limb:** He accepts the indignity. He lets Sue sit beside a hospital bed and feed him ice chips. He permits the role-reversal that is the final intimacy a parent can give a grown child — *be needed by me*. This is the deepest possible reparation, because it allows his children to do for him what he could not do for Mary, and to do it without failing.
- **Catastrophe limb:** He hides the diagnosis. He arranges to die off-world, alone, in a manner that spares his children the bedside. He frames this as a kindness. It is, in fact, the last cut of the original wound: he denies them, one final time, the ordinary work of loving a father.

---

### 3. Push Vectors Toward Growth

Specifying what would actually move the subject, in descending order of plausible force:

- **A direct, undeflectable request from Sue.** Not "please come home" — which he can refuse on protective grounds — but "I need you to do this small ordinary thing, and only you can do it." His pressure point is his children's safety and his children's *asked-for* need. Framing must convert his desire to atone from the heroic register to the domestic one.
- **A grandchild's unmediated affection.** As above. The very young are the only humans on the board against whom he has no developed defense, because his entire defensive structure is calibrated against the *judgment* of those who knew his fall, and children do not know it.
- **Sustained therapeutic contact with a peer who has survived an analogous event.** Another physician who lost a patient who was kin, ideally one who chose the harder path of staying. Franklin is unlikely to accept help from below or from authority, but he might accept it from a fellow practitioner who has walked the same corridor.
- **Removal of the heroic option.** A circumstance in which there is *no bomb to leap on* and the only available form of love is the slow kind. Long convalescence of a family member. A grandchild's chronic illness requiring repeated, unspectacular presence. The subject's growth depends, ironically, on being denied his preferred defense.
- **Mary, addressed by name, repeatedly, by people who loved her.** The unprocessed wound must be defrosted at the rate of ordinary conversation. Photographs. Anecdotes. The simple, unforced re-introduction of her into the household discourse.

---

### 4. Push Vectors Toward Catastrophe

In rough order of acuteness:

- **Any clean opportunity for self-sacrifice.** Hand him a bomb and a familial threat and he will take the bomb. The arrangement of his environment to *minimize the availability of such moments* is the single most important external safeguard.
- **A second iatrogenic failure.** If Franklin is in a position to operate on a loved one again and that operation fails — or even goes poorly — the recapitulation of the original wound will likely produce acute, possibly fatal decompensation. He should not, under any circumstance, be the surgeon of record for any family member, including grandchildren. Not because his hands are not capable — they are — but because his psyche is not.
- **Renewed substance access during a stressor.** He has demonstrated that alcohol, in him, is not a primary appetite but a grief-anesthetic. Reintroduction in the context of a fresh loss (Sue endangered, Johnny lost, Mary's anniversary in an unsupported context) would likely reignite the full collapse sequence.
- **Isolation framed as service.** The most insidious catastrophe vector, because it disguises itself as growth. A posting to a distant clinic where he is "doing good." This is the pattern, not its disruption. The dossier should be alert to the subject's gift for converting flight into vocation.
- **Hagiographic framing by his children.** If Sue or Johnny, out of love, treat him as already-redeemed — if they paper over the failures rather than name them — they will inadvertently lock him in the very martyr role he uses to avoid the harder work. The most loving thing they can do is to be, in some measured degree, *ordinary* with him: to ask things of him, to be annoyed with him, to let him be late and forgive him for it. To treat him as a father, not a relic.

---

### 5. Open Questions

The following are unresolved and forward-determinative:

- **Has the subject ever, in private, said Mary's name aloud since her death?** The answer to this question would substantially update the prognosis in either direction. The behavioral record neither confirms nor denies.
- **Does Sue want him back, or does she want the *idea* of him back?** These are different reunions and produce different fathers. Sue's own clarity on this question is rate-limiting for his recovery.
- **What does Johnny think?** Johnny has historically been the less-narrativized child in relation to Franklin. His unprocessed material — being raised by a sister rather than a parent — is its own dossier, and his eventual collision with Franklin (rather than reconciliation) may be the more catalytic event for the father's growth than any quiet scene with Sue.
- **Is there a version of Franklin who can tolerate being thanked?** Currently, the answer appears to be no — he metabolizes gratitude as further evidence of debt. Until he can simply receive thanks, no relational repair will hold.
- **What would he do if he learned he was *not*, in any technical sense, responsible for Mary's death?** New evidence — a previously-unknown cardiac anomaly, an unsurvivable injury, anything that medically exonerates the surgeon-of-record — would present him with the most destabilizing data of his life. It would not heal him automatically; it might in fact make things worse before better, because his entire post-Mary identity is scaffolded on the guilt. He would have to grieve again, this time without the consolation of having had a job to do about it.

---

### 6. Probability-Weighted Forecast

Synthesizing the above into a single distribution over outcomes for the subject's next operational chapter:

- **~55% — Repetition.** Another cycle of remote service, reluctant reunion, brief intimacy, and sacrificial exit. The most likely outcome because it is the established pattern and nothing in his environment has yet been configured to disrupt it.
- **~20% — Stalled middle.** Survival without growth. He returns, stays nearby, practices medicine in some modest capacity, never has the Mary conversation, never fully arrives. Functions as a quiet presence at family events. Dies eventually of ordinary causes, leaving his children with a softer but still unresolved father. Better than repetition; not what he or they need.
- **~15% — Partial reparation.** He achieves real contact with grandchildren and a working, if guarded, peace with Sue. The Mary wound remains largely unaddressed but no longer governs his geography. He dies as an actual grandfather. This is the realistic best case.
- **~7% — Full reparation.** He does the work. He talks about Mary. He stays. He ages into ordinary mortality and lets his children love him through it. He becomes, late and incompletely but truly, the father he was not. Low probability, and worth every effort on the part of those around him.
- **~3% — Acute catastrophe.** Decompensation under a re-triggering event (a second surgical failure, a child's near-death he could not prevent), producing rapid relapse and a final, unredemptive death. Lowest probability but worth naming because it is the failure mode against which the most concrete safeguards can be erected.

---

### 7. Closing Observation

The subject is, at this stage of his life, a man who has been *given more chances than the universe normally allots*, and who has spent each of them on a more refined version of the same refusal. The forward question is not whether he will get another chance — the structure of his world suggests he will — but whether anyone, including himself, will recognize the chance for what it is: an invitation to do the small, unphotographed, unredemptive work of sitting in a kitchen with his daughter and being known.

He has saved the world by dying. He has not yet tried to save himself by staying. That remains, against the weight of sixty years of pattern, the one experiment he has not run.

The dossier will be updated when he does — or, more probably, when he doesn't.

## Relationship Graph
### Susan Storm
- The only durable tether. She retains more of the truth than Johnny and grieves him cleanly - evidence the pre-fall father was real and warm.
- His pattern with her is protective concealment: tells her less than she can handle, in the doctor's habit of rationing bad news.
- She inherits his over-responsibility, his absorbing of cost in silence, his conflict-avoidance in family matters.
- Failure mode: were he to survive and remain present, the concealment would corrode her trust; she would eventually demand the full account and his refusal would read as the second abandonment. Leverage: any credible threat to Sue collapses every other consideration in him.

### Jonathan Storm
- Younger at the time of collapse; memories sparser, more idealized, more brittle.
- Inherits the unmetabolized grief in acted-out form: recklessness as a way of daring mortality.
- Franklin's protective instinct toward Johnny is undifferentiated and absolute - he would die for him without calculation.
- Failure mode: confronted with the full truth of his father's choices, Johnny is the one more likely to break - the idealization cannot bend. Leverage: threats to Johnny move Franklin identically to threats to Sue.

### [[Reed Richards (Mister Fantastic)]]
- Brief acquaintance, largely in Franklin's degraded state. Franklin dies absorbing a blast meant for Reed.
- Reed names his firstborn 'Franklin' (FF Annual #6) - the highest honor Reed could pay a man he barely knew, evidence Reed read the moral clarity of the final act and the surgeon's residual competence as the true man.
- Franklin regards Reed with deference bordering on gratitude - the man who took the post he abdicated.
- Failure mode: a longer relationship would have tested whether Reed's reverence could survive Franklin's compulsive self-erasure; Reed's tendency to fix problems would have collided with Franklin's refusal to be fixed. Leverage: invoking Reed and Sue's family - especially Franklin Jr. - is the one frame that could induce Franklin to accept care rather than refuse it.

### Mary Storm
- Deceased wife. The organizing internal object. Every post-fall behavior is addressed, in some register, to her.
- He cannot say her name without cost; he will not visit her grave on panel; he keeps her in the room by keeping her unspoken.
- Failure mode: not a relationship that can curdle - it is already the wound. Leverage: any reminder destabilizes; weaponized reminders (anniversary, image, voice) would shatter the constricted affect that holds him together.

### The Skrulls
- Captors and somatic violators. Identified, correctly, that he would accept being remade into the face of an enemy because he already believed he was one.
- Operational lesson: he is exploitable by any party willing to offer him a 'clean' way to be removed from his children's lives.
- Failure mode: the template - coerce him by routing through his children, and he complies. Leverage runs through Sue and Johnny, always.

### The Creditor He Killed
- The man whose death he never stopped paying for. The act was situational, not patterned, but Franklin metabolized it as confirmation of the bad-object self-concept.
- Operational note: he accepted maximum moral weight rather than mitigation; this is the template for every subsequent decision.
